Proof from Composition of Opposites
Maturidi argues from the combination of contrary natures in perceptible things to their createdness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the combination of contrary natures in perceptible things proves their createdness and dependence on a Creator.

Core Idea
Opposites that naturally repel cannot unite by themselves; their union proves a Creator.

Maturidi presents a concise yet profound proof for the origination of the world based on a simple observation: everything we perceive is made up of elements that by nature are opposed to each other. Why do they stay together? The answer points directly to a cause beyond themselves.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the logical flow from observation to conclusion.
The passage is a single sentence but contains multiple premises.
2
Identify key terms
Understand terms like 'محسوس' (perceptible), 'طبائع' (natures), 'مضادة' (contrary), 'تنافر' (repulsion), and 'اجتماع' (combination).
These terms are essential for following the argument.
3
Trace the argument
Follow the reasoning: every perceptible thing contains different and contrary natures → those natures naturally repel → their combination must be from something else → therefore the thing is originated.
This is a simple cause-effect chain.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this proves createdness. If something were eternal, it would not require an external cause for its composition.
5
Check understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to test if you grasped the core reasoning.
The answer is directly from the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن كل محسوس لا يخلو عن اجتماع طبائع مختلفة ومتضادة مما حقها التنافر والتباعد لأنفسها ، ثبت اجتماعها بغيرها ، وفي ذلك حدثه ، والله الموفق
And also that every perceptible thing is not free from the combination of different and contrary natures, whose due of themselves is repulsion and distance. Their combination is established by something else, and in that is its origination. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage is a concise proof from the composition of opposites. The author observes that all perceptible bodies are composed of various and even contrary natures (e.g., hot and cold, wet and dry). By their own essence, these natures would tend to repel and separate. The fact that they are actually combined indicates the action of an external agent that brings them together. This combination is therefore not self-caused, implying that the composite entity is originated (ḥādith). The proof is based on the principle that if something were eternal, it would have to be self-sufficient; but composition from opposing elements shows dependence on an external assembler.

Key Terms
محسوس
طبائع
مختلفة
مضادة
تنافر
اجتماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that composition of elements does not imply an external cause because mixtures can occur naturally.
Correction: Maturidi points out that the natures involved are contrary and naturally repel, so their combination cannot be self-caused; it requires an external agent.

Checkpoint
Why does the combination of different and contrary natures in perceptible things indicate origination?
A) Because opposites cannot coexist eternally.
B) Because the combination requires an external agent.
C) Because the natures are inherently repulsive.
D) Because all perceptible things are temporal.

Key Takeaway
The coexistence of opposite natures in perceptible things proves they are brought together by an external cause, and thus they are originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Look at your own life: where do you experience conflicting desires or responsibilities that you cannot reconcile on your own? Have you ever paused to see that this very tension points to a Higher Power holding you together? What would it look like to entrust that tension to Him today?
?
If every harmonious moment in your life—peace amidst chaos, unity in diversity—is a sign that an External Agent sustains it, then where are you acting as if you are the source of your own wholeness? Will you acknowledge the Giver in the midst of the gift?
?
The source says opposites 'by themselves' repel. In your spiritual state, what 'opposites' do you ignore or suppress—faith and doubt, hope and fear, love and apathy—rather than bringing them before the One who alone can unite them? What step can you take this week to bring them to Him?

Argument from Parts and Growth
Maturidi argues from parts and growth to the whole's origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's proof that the temporal origination of the world's parts and their growth implies the origination of the whole world.

Core Idea
If parts are born and grow, the whole cannot be eternal.

This passage presents a key argument from early kalam: the argument from composition and growth. Maturidi observes that we see parts of the world coming into existence and growing. Since the whole is nothing but the combination of these parts, the whole must also have a beginning. This argument connects observable change to the createdness of the entire universe.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage is concise and uses technical terms like أجزاء and أبعاض.
2
Identify the two premises
The argument has two main premises: (1) most parts of the world are known to be originated after not existing, and (2) growth, expansion, and increase are observed. The conclusion is that the whole must be originated.
The final clause about finite parts not becoming infinite supports the conclusion.
3
Reflect on the logic
Ask yourself: if individual parts come into existence and grow, how could the entire collection be eternal? This is the core of the argument.
This connects to the learning objective and the common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن العالم ذو أجزاء وأبعاض ، ويُعلم أكثر أبعاضه أنه حادث بعد أن لم يكن ، ويعلم نماوه واتساعه وكبره ، لزم ذلك فى كله ؛ إذ لا يصير اجتماع أجزاء متناهية غير متناهية
And also that the world possesses parts and limbs. Most of its limbs are known to be originated after not having been, and its growth, expansion, and increase are known. Therefore that applies to the whole; because the combination of finite parts cannot be infinite.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage uses the argument from composition and growth. The author states that the world has parts (ajzāʾ) and members (aʿḍāʾ). Many of these parts are known to have come into existence after not existing (e.g., the growth of animals, plants, etc.). Moreover, we observe growth, expansion, and increase in size. If parts of the world are originated, then the whole world, which is the collection of these parts, must also be originated. The final clause 'because the combination of finite parts cannot be infinite' is a bit obscure; it may mean that if the parts are finite and originated, the whole cannot be eternal (infinite in duration). Alternatively, it could be a gloss about the impossibility of an infinite regress of parts. The core logic is that the temporal origination of the part implies the temporal origination of the whole.

Key Terms
أجزاء
أبعاض
نمو
اتساع
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the whole world could be eternal even though its parts change and grow.
Correction: Maturidi argues that if the parts are originated and constantly arising, the aggregate cannot be eternal because the combination of finite, originated parts cannot yield an infinite (eternal) whole.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi conclude that the whole world must be originated from the origination of its parts?
A) Because parts are finite and cannot be infinite.
B) Because the whole is nothing but the sum of its parts.
C) Because growth and expansion are observed.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
The world's parts and their observable growth demonstrate that the whole universe is created and not eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You see your own body grow and change daily. Have you ever truly paused to consider that every cell of your being is a witness that you are created—and that the One who created you from nothing is rightfully your Lord? What would change in your prayer, your trust, your fear of Him if you felt that reality right now?
?
The world around you appears permanent, yet this lesson shows that its parts are constantly arising. You know the world will end, but do you live as if it will last forever? Name one attachment to this world that you hold onto as if it is eternal—and then ask yourself: is that thing truly worthy of being your ultimate concern?
?
If the combination of finite parts cannot be infinite, then everything you rely on is finite. Your health, your wealth, your relationships—all are composed of temporary parts. What have you placed your ultimate hope in? Is it something that will perish? Let this thought drive you to anchor your hope only in the Eternal.

The Proof from Change and Diversity
Maturidi enumerates opposites, argues from change to annihilation, refutes an objection, and concludes with divine dependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that observable diversity and change in the world prove its temporal origination and contingency, and thus the existence of a necessary Creator.

Core Idea
Change and opposites show the world is not eternal; only the Eternal is unchanging.

Maturidi invites us to look at the world around us: good and bad, light and darkness, small and large. These opposites are not fixed; they change and pass away. This simple observation, he argues, reveals that the world cannot be eternal. In this lesson, we will walk through his proof step by step, seeing how change leads to annihilation, and how annihilation points to a beginning and a Creator.

Guided Path
1
Notice the opposites
Read the first sentence where Maturidi lists pairs of opposites. These are observable facts that everyone can see. Why do you think he starts with these examples?
The pairs cover moral, physical, and aesthetic dimensions.
2
Understand the implication of change
Maturidi says these pairs are signs of change and passing away. Change leads to annihilation and destruction. Reflect on why change necessarily implies a potential for non-existence.
If something changes, it is not immutable; what is mutable can cease to be.
3
The combination and dispersion argument
He gives an example: combination strengthens, dispersion weakens. When a thing disperses, it becomes void. This is a sign of annihilation. Think about how this supports the idea that the world is not self-subsistent.
This is reminiscent of the argument from composition.
4
Refute the objection
Maturidi addresses an objection: someone might claim that God is hidden from sight, implying something about eternity. He dismisses this, saying that the world is known by sight, not by such claims. See how this refutation strengthens his proof.
The objection is a straw man; Maturidi cuts it down quickly.
5
Conclude with the source of strength
The final sentence: 'There is no difference between a life that perishes and its essence. And that has not ceased; its strength is only with Allah.' This ties everything back to Allah as the only eternal and self-sufficient being.
The proof ends by affirming tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن منه طيب وحبيث [؟] ، وصغير وكبير ، وحسن وقبيح ، ونور وظلمة ، وهذه آيات التغير والزوال ، وفى التغير والزوال فناء وهلاك ؛ إذ معلوم أن الإجتماع يؤكد ويقوى ويعظم ، دليله النشر ، وأنه إذا تفرق بطل ذلك ، أن ذلك آية الفناء ، وما احتمل الفناء لم يجز كونه بنفسه ويلزم أيضا احتمال الابتداء ، وليس لقول من يقول : يغيب عن الأبصار ولا يعنى معنى ، لما علم العالم بالبصر لا بالدلائل ، وبه يُدعى القدم ، فقد مع ما أنا بينا من وهنه ، ولا فرق بين حياة يفنى وبين ذاته ، ولا زال ذلك قوه إلا بالله
And also that from it are good and bad, small and large, beautiful and ugly, light and darkness. These are signs of change and passing away. In change and passing away there is annihilation and destruction, for it is known that combination strengthens, fortifies, and magnifies – its proof is spreading – and that when it disperses, that becomes void. That is a sign of annihilation, and what is susceptible to annihilation cannot exist by itself. Also the possibility of beginning follows necessarily. And the saying of one who says 'He is hidden from eyes' is meaningless, because the world is known by sight, not by proofs, and by it eternity is claimed. So it has fallen along with what we have shown of its weakness. There is no difference between a life that perishes and its essence. And that has not ceased; its strength is only with Allah.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from the observable diversity and change in the world. The author notes that the world contains opposites: good and bad, small and large, light and darkness. These are signs of change (taghayyur) and passing (zawāl). Change implies eventual annihilation (fanāʾ) and destruction (halāk). The author argues that combination strengthens, but dispersion leads to dissolution. If something is susceptible to annihilation, it cannot exist by itself (i.e., it is not self-subsistent). Moreover, the possibility of a beginning is also necessary. The author then refutes an objection that God might be hidden from sight, saying that this does not prove eternity; rather, the world's changeability shows weakness. Even a life that perishes cannot be eternal. The final phrase emphasizes that all strength comes from Allah. This proof is based on the principle that any entity subject to change cannot be eternal, because eternity implies immutability.

زوال
فناء
هلاك
اجتماع

ابتداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that change is only superficial and does not affect the essence of things, so the world could still be eternal.
Correction: Maturidi argues that change indicates a real potential for annihilation, which is incompatible with eternity. Anything subject to change cannot be self-subsistent and must have a beginning.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi consider the presence of opposites (like light/darkness) as evidence that the world is not eternal?
A) Because opposites cannot exist in the same place.
B) Because they are signs of change and passing away, which imply annihilation.
C) Because they prove that God is hidden from sight.
D) Because combination strengthens and dispersion weakens.

Key Takeaway
The observable diversity and change in the world prove that it is not eternal; only Allah, the Creator, is self-subsistent and unchanging.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

In which area of your life are you still living as though your stability comes from your own resources, rather than from Allah? What concrete step will you take today to shift that dependence to Him?
?
Maturidi dismisses the claim 'God is hidden from sight' as meaningless when used to argue for eternity. Is there any excuse or assumption you have been using to avoid facing your own finitude and need for Allah? What would it cost you to truly accept that you are nothing without Him?
?
The lesson ends with the truth: 'its strength is only with Allah.' Think of the one thing that currently weighs most heavily on your heart. If that strength belongs solely to Allah, how should your worry change right now? What would it look like to hand that burden to Him completely before you sleep tonight?

Proof from Alternation of Motion and Rest
Maturidi uses motion-rest alternation to prove temporality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the alternation between motion and rest in a body proves its temporal origination.

Core Idea
Opposites can't be eternal together, so the body that alternates must be created.

Maturidi begins a logical proof from the observable fact that every physical body is never free from either motion or rest. Since these two states are opposites that cannot coexist simultaneously, the body must experience both over time. From this alternation, he deduces that the body is temporal and not eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
This is a short but dense argument.
2
Identify the key premise
Note that the argument starts with the fact that a body is always in motion or rest, and that these two cannot combine. Why is this significant?
3
Understand the implication of 'half'
Maturidi says that over time, half the body's moments are motion and half are rest. Something with halves is finite. Connect this to the idea that the body's existence must have a beginning.
This shows that the body cannot be eternal.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that the body is originated (hadith). Ask yourself: what would happen if motion and rest were both eternal? Would that be possible?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى ذلك طريق علم الاستدلال ، مع ما أنه لا يخلو الجسم من حركة أو سكون ، وليس لها الإجتماع ، فيزول من جملة أوقاته نصف الحركة ونصف السكون، وكل ذى نصف متناه ، على أنها إذ لا يجتمعان في القدم لزم حدث أحد الوجهين ، ويبطلانه أن يكون محدثا فى الأزل لزم فى الآخر ، وفي ذلك حدث ما لا يخلو عنه. وأيضا أن كل جسم لا يخلو عن سكون دائم أو حركة دائمة أو هما وما هو عليه منهما مدفوع إليه مسخر به ومجعول لمنافع غيره ، وإذا كان ذلك وصف جواهر العالم التى لا توصف بالحياة ثبت أنها محدثة ؛ إذ هي لا على ما ولكن على تسخيرها وتذليلها واستعمالها فى حوائج غيرها . وإذا ثبت ذلك في أصل هنى بنفسها
And upon that is the way of the science of inference, along with that the body is not free from motion or rest, and they do not have combination. So there disappears from its total times half of motion and half of rest, and everything that has a half is finite, because they do not combine in eternity, so the origination of one of the two aspects follows. And they invalidate that it could be originated in pre-eternity, for it would follow in the other. And in that is the origination of what it never free from. And also that every body is not free from constant rest or constant motion or both, and what it is upon of them is driven to it, subjugated by it, and made for the benefit of others. And if that is the description of the substances of the world that are not described with life, it is established that they are originated, because they are not upon their own, but upon their subjugation, taming, and use in the needs of others. And if that is established in the origin, it itself has [؟].
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage contains two related proofs from motion and rest. The first proof: every body (jism) is never free from either motion or rest. Since motion and rest are opposites that cannot coexist simultaneously, at any given time the body is either in motion or at rest. Over time, the body experiences both states. The author argues that because the body alternates between motion and rest, and each of these states is finite in duration (since they occupy half of the time, implying finitude), the body itself must be originated. Moreover, if motion and rest cannot both be eternal (since they are opposite and one would have to be eternal and the other temporal), the body that changes from one to the other cannot be eternal. The second proof: every body is subject to either constant motion, constant rest, or both. But whatever state it is in, it is driven to it and subjugated for the benefit of others. This subjugation indicates that bodies are not self-sufficient; they are used for the needs of other things. Therefore, the substances (jawāhir) of the world, which are not alive, are proven to be originated. The final clause suggests that this is established in their very essence.

Key Terms
حركة
سكون
جسم
نصف
قدم
حدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that motion and rest could both be eternal in a body.
Correction: Maturidi argues they cannot coexist in eternity because they are opposites; therefore the body that undergoes both must be temporal.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi conclude from the fact that a body alternates between motion and rest?
A) The body is eternal.
B) The body must be originated.
C) Motion and rest are both eternal.
D) The body has infinite duration.

Key Takeaway
A body's alternation between motion and rest proves it is temporal, not eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your body constantly moves and rests—this very alternation proves it is created and dependent on the Creator. When you feel exhausted or restless, do you recognize your need for the Eternal One? How would your daily prayers change if you truly felt this dependence?
?
This proof shows that nothing physical can be eternal. What material things—possessions, relationships, or goals—do you treat as if they will last forever? What would it cost you to loosen your grip on them?
?
The fact that your body alternates between motion and rest is not just biology; it is a sign of your temporality. Are you living as though this world is your permanent home? What concrete action can you take today to remind yourself that your ultimate abode is with the Eternal?

Proof from Subjugation and Dependence
Maturidi argues from subjugation to temporal origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the subjugation of bodies for others' benefits indicates they are contingent and created.

Core Idea
Bodies are driven and used for others, so they are not self-sufficient but created.

Maturidi presents a second argument: every body is either constantly in motion, constantly at rest, or both, and in any case it is subjugated (musakhkhar) and made for the benefit of other things. This dependence shows that bodies are not self-causing but are temporal substances (jawāhir) created by a Maker.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Note the term 'tashīr' (subjugation) which is key.
2
Identify the condition of bodies
Maturidi says every body is in constant motion, constant rest, or both. This is a three-way categorization. Notice that in any case, the state is not self-chosen.
3
Understand 'subjugation'
The state is described as 'madfūʿ ilayh' (driven to it) and 'musakhkhar bih' (subjugated by it) and 'majʿūl li manāfiʿ ghayrih' (made for the benefit of others). This implies external control and purpose.
Contrast with a living being that acts for its own purpose.
4
Connect to temporal origination
Since bodies are subjugated, they are not self-standing. This proves they are originated (muhdatha). Ask: why does subjugation imply origination?

Source Text

Proof from Dependence on Another
Maturidi's proof from necessary dependence on another.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that anything depending on something else for its existence must be temporal, not eternal.

Core Idea
Dependence on another proves temporality.

Maturidi offers a concise logical proof: everything in the sensible world exists only through another. Since true eternity (qidam) precludes dependence, such things must be created. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the flow.
Focus on the terms الغير, الحدث, القدم.
2
Identify the premises
Break the argument into premise: 'nothing exists except by another', and the derived conclusion: 'therefore it is temporal'.
Notice why the author states that pre-eternity prevents existence by another.
3
Reflect on the logic
Ask yourself: why does dependence negate pre-eternity? The key is that pre-eternity implies self-sufficiency.
Consider how this proof relies on the definition of qidam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنه لم يكن واحد منها إلا بغيره ، وإذا ثبت الغير لزم الحدث ، إذ القدم يمنع الكون لغيره وأيضا أن كل محسوس لا يخلو عن اجتماع طبائع مختلفة ومتضادة مما حقها التنافر والتباعد لأنفسها ، ثبت اجتماعها بغيرها ، وفي ذلك حدثه ، والله الموفق
That none of them existed except by another, and if the other is established, then temporality (al-ḥadath) is necessary, for pre-eternity (al-qidam) prevents existence by another. And also that every sensible thing is not free from the conjunction of different and opposing natures, whose right is mutual repulsion and distance by themselves; their conjunction is established by another, and in that is its temporality, and God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage presents two brief proofs for the temporality (ḥudūth) of the world. The first proof is from dependency: nothing in the world exists except by something else. If a thing depends on another for its existence, then it cannot be pre-eternal (qadīm), because pre-eternity negates being through another. Therefore, such dependent things are temporal. The second proof is from the composition of contradictory natures in sensible objects. Every perceptible object consists of various natures that are naturally incompatible and tend to separate. Their actual conjunction, therefore, cannot come from themselves but must be imposed by an external agent. This external composition indicates that the object is temporal (ḥādith). The passage ends with 'wa Allāhu al-muwaffiq' (God is the granter of success), a common pious formula concluding a proof.

Key Terms
الغير (al-ghayr)
الحدث (al-ḥadath)
القدم (al-qidam)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if something is dependent, it could still be eternal if the thing it depends on is also eternal.
Correction: Maturidi asserts that pre-eternity (qidam) by its very nature implies self-sufficiency. If a thing depends on another, it is not self-sufficient and therefore cannot be pre-eternal.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does dependence on another (al-ghayr) necessitate temporality (al-ḥadath)?
A) Because all things are created by God
B) Because pre-eternity prevents existence through another
C) Because nothing can depend on itself
D) Because the world is composed of opposites

Key Takeaway
Dependence on another is a clear sign of contingency and temporality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that anything dependent on another cannot be eternal. Look at your own life: what are you depending on right now that you treat as if it will never go away? How does this lesson expose the lie behind that attachment?
?
If your very existence hangs on Allah's will every moment, why do you often live as if you are self-sufficient? What practical change can you make today to remind yourself of your constant need for Him?
?
The proof shows that dependence proves temporality. You will not last forever. What would you change about your priorities if you truly believed that every second of your existence is a gift from Another?

Proof from Composition of Opposing Natures
Maturidi's proof from the composition of contradictory natures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the conjunction of opposing natures in sensible objects proves they are created.

Core Idea
Opposing natures cannot unite by themselves.

Maturidi's second proof observes that every physical object contains multiple, often conflicting, natures. Since these natures naturally repel each other, their coming together must be caused by an external agent. This lesson traces the logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation together. Note the emphasis on 'different and opposing natures'.
Pay attention to the phrase 'حقها التنافر والتباعد لأنفسها'.
2
Understand the natural state
Recognize that the inherent tendency of opposing natures is mutual repulsion and distance. They do not naturally come together.
Think of examples like fire and water, hot and cold.
3
Draw the conclusion
Since the natures are found together in every sensible thing, their conjunction must come from an external cause, proving the object is temporal.
The phrase 'ثبت اجتماعها بغيرها' is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنه لم يكن واحد منها إلا بغيره ، وإذا ثبت الغير لزم الحدث ، إذ القدم يمنع الكون لغيره وأيضا أن كل محسوس لا يخلو عن اجتماع طبائع مختلفة ومتضادة مما حقها التنافر والتباعد لأنفسها ، ثبت اجتماعها بغيرها ، وفي ذلك حدثه ، والله الموفق
That none of them existed except by another, and if the other is established, then temporality (al-ḥadath) is necessary, for pre-eternity (al-qidam) prevents existence by another. And also that every sensible thing is not free from the conjunction of different and opposing natures, whose right is mutual repulsion and distance by themselves; their conjunction is established by another, and in that is its temporality, and God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage presents two brief proofs for the temporality (ḥudūth) of the world. The first proof is from dependency: nothing in the world exists except by something else. If a thing depends on another for its existence, then it cannot be pre-eternal (qadīm), because pre-eternity negates being through another. Therefore, such dependent things are temporal. The second proof is from the composition of contradictory natures in sensible objects. Every perceptible object consists of various natures that are naturally incompatible and tend to separate. Their actual conjunction, therefore, cannot come from themselves but must be imposed by an external agent. This external composition indicates that the object is temporal (ḥādith). The passage ends with 'wa Allāhu al-muwaffiq' (God is the granter of success), a common pious formula concluding a proof.

Key Terms
اجتماع الطبائع (ijtimāʿ al-ṭabāʾiʿ)
التنافر (al-tanāfur)
التباعد (al-tabāʿud)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that opposing natures can naturally combine, like in chemical mixtures.
Correction: Maturidi argues from the inherent nature of opposites: they tend to separate. The fact that they remain together in a single object shows an external force is at work.

Checkpoint
What proves that the conjunction of opposing natures in sensible objects is caused by another?
A) The fact that they naturally attract
B) The fact that they naturally repel each other
C) The fact that they are eternal
D) The fact that they are visible

Key Takeaway
The unity of opposites in every physical thing points to an external creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You see your own body—a composition of countless opposing systems and chemicals. Who holds them together? When was the last time you truly thanked the One who prevents your atoms from flying apart?
?
When you feel internal conflicts pulling you in different directions, do you remember that only Allah can unite your heart? What step will you take today to seek His help in bringing your scattered intentions together?
?
You encounter countless composite objects every day—from your phone to your family. This proof says each one silently testifies to a Creator. Will you let yourself hear that testimony, or will you remain deaf to it?

Proof from Parts, Growth, and Opposites
Maturidi presents two proofs for the temporality of the world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the existence of parts, growth, and opposites in the world to argue for its temporality and dependence on a Creator.

Core Idea
Parts that change and opposites that conflict cannot be eternal.

Maturidi presents two interconnected proofs drawn from everyday observation: the world is made of parts that grow and change, and it contains opposites like light and darkness. These features show that the world is temporal and cannot exist by itself. Let's examine his reasoning carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text slowly. Notice the structure: first argument about parts and growth, then argument about opposites. Don't worry about the fragmented sentence.
The ellipsis 'لا يصير . . اجتماع أجزاء متناهية غير متناهية' is likely a lacuna in the manuscript; the main point remains clear.
2
Understand the first proof
Maturidi argues that most parts of the world are known to have originated after not existing. Since the whole depends on its parts, the whole must also be temporal.
3
Understand the second proof
The presence of opposites (good/bad, light/darkness) indicates change and passing away, which lead to annihilation. Anything that can be annihilated cannot exist by itself.
4
Connect to the main conclusion
Both arguments converge on the same point: the world is not self-subsistent; it is created and depends on a Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن العالم ذو أجزاء وأبعاض ، ويُعلم أكثر أبعاضه أنه حادث بعد أن لم يكن ، ويعلم نماوه واتساعه وكبره ، لزم ذلك فى كله ؛ إذ لا يصير . . اجتماع أجزاء متناهية غير متناهية وأيضا أن منه طيب وخبيث ، وصغير وكبير ، وحسن وقبيح ، ونور وظلمة ، وهذه آيات التغير والزوال ، وفى التغير والزوال فناء وهلاك ؛ إذ معلوم أن الإجتماع يؤكد ويقوى ويعظم ، دليله النشر ، وأنه إذا تفرق بطل ذلك ، أن ذلك آية الفناء ، وما احتمل الفناء لم يجز كونه بنفسه
And also that the world possesses parts and limbs, and most of its parts are known to be temporally originated (ḥādith) after not having been, and its growth, expansion, and bigness are known; so that is necessary for the whole, for it is not... conjunction of finite parts infinite. And also that within it are good and bad, small and large, beautiful and ugly, light and darkness, and these are signs of change and passing away, and in change and passing away are annihilation and destruction; for it is known that conjunction strengthens, reinforces, and magnifies – its proof is spreading – and that when it separates, that ceases; that is a sign of annihilation, and whatever admits annihilation cannot exist by itself.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage presents two interrelated proofs. First, the world has parts and limbs (aʿḍāʾ) and many of its parts are known to have originated after not existing; additionally, phenomena like growth, expansion, and increase in size are observed. Since the whole depends on its parts, the whole must also be temporal. The text then introduces a second proof from the presence of opposites within the world: good and bad, small and large, beautiful and ugly, light and darkness. These opposites are evidence of change and passing away (zawāl), which imply annihilation (fanāʾ) and destruction. The author argues that composition (ijtimāʿ) strengthens and magnifies things, but when components separate, the composite ceases to exist. Therefore, anything that can undergo annihilation cannot be self-subsistent or eternal; it must be temporal.

Key Terms
أجزاء (ajzāʾ)
أبعاض (abʿāḍ)
الحادث (al-ḥādith)
الفناء (al-fanāʾ)
التغير (al-taghayyur)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might argue that parts can be eternal if the whole is eternal.
Correction: Maturidi counters by noting that parts themselves are observed to originate temporally (e.g., growth of limbs), so the whole cannot be eternal.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what do opposites like light and darkness indicate about the world?
A) They show the world was created by two gods
B) They are signs of change and passing away
C) They prove the world is eternal
D) They have no significance

Key Takeaway
The world's parts, growth, and opposites show it is temporal and cannot exist by itself; thus it must have a Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every part of this world you rely on—your body, your possessions, even the ground you stand on—is subject to change and annihilation, why do you still anchor your security in them rather than in the Eternal who created them?
?
Maturidi argues that opposites like light and darkness are signs of change and passing away. Look at your own life: where do you see opposites—joy and sorrow, strength and weakness—and how do they remind you that your current state is not permanent? Will you use that reminder to turn to the One who never changes?
?
The proof concludes that whatever admits annihilation cannot exist by itself. You will one day cease. If you are not self-existent, then who are you truly dependent upon? Have you lived today as if that dependence is your only reality?

Refuting Hidden Eternity and Proving Temporality from Motion and Rest
Maturidi refutes hidden eternity and gives motion-rest proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the claim that the world's pre-eternity is hidden from observation, and his proof from the alternation of motion and rest that bodies must have a temporal beginning.

Core Idea
What alternates between opposites cannot be eternal.

Maturidi begins by countering an objection: some argue that the world's eternity is not perceptible, so it cannot be disproved. He responds that the world is known both by sight and by proofs. Then he presents a powerful rational argument from motion and rest—since every body alternates between these two states, each must occupy half of time, and anything divisible into halves is finite. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage from 'ويلزم أيضا' up to 'في ذلك حدث ما لا يخلو عنه' (the first part).
The text is dense due to OCR issues.
2
Identify the refutation
Find where Maturidi responds to the claim that pre-eternity is hidden. Notice his counter: the world is known by sight and proofs.
3
Follow the motion-rest argument
Trace the steps: body always has motion or rest, they cannot coexist, each occupies half of its time, half implies finitude, thus the body cannot be pre-eternal.
This is a classic kalam argument.
4
Ask why alternation is key
Consider why alternation forces temporality. If motion and rest were both eternal, they would have to exist simultaneously, which is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويلزم أيضا احتمال الابتداء ، وليس لقول من يقول : يغيب عن الأبصار ولا يعنى معنى ، لما علم العالم بالبصر لا بالدلائل ، وبه يُدعى القدم ، فقد مع ما أنا بينا من وهنه ، ولا فرق بين حياة يفنى وبين ذاته ، ولا زال ذلك قوه إلا بالله وعلى ذلك طريق علم الاستدلال ، مع ما أنه لا يخلو الجسم من حركة أو سكون ، وليس لها الإجتماع ، فيزول من جملة أوقاته نصف الحركة ونصف السكون، وكل ذى نصف متناه ، على أنها إذ لا يجتمعان في القدم لزم حدث أحد الوجهين ، ويبطلانه أن / يكون محدثا فى الأزل لزم فى الآخر ، وفي ذلك حدث ما لا يخلو عنه. وأيضا أن كل جسم لا يخلو عن سكون دائم أو حركة دائمة أو هما وما هو عليه منهما مدفوع إليه مسخر به ومجعول لمنافع غيره ، وإذا كان ذلك وصف جواهر العالم التى لا توصف بالحياة ثبت أنها محدثة ؛ إذ هي لا على ما ولكن على تسخيرها وتذليلها واستعمالها فى حوائج غيرها . وإذا ثبت ذلك في أصل هنى بنفسها فكذلك الجواهر والأحياء الذين هم فيها وبها تقر وننتفع وهم مجبولون والمنافع أحق بذلك ، والله الموفق
And also necessary is the possibility of beginning, and not for the saying of one who says: it is hidden from sight and has no meaning, because the world is known by sight, not by proofs, and by that pre-eternity is claimed – it has indeed, along with what we have shown of its weakness, no difference between a life that perishes and its essence, and that state of its strength only through God. And upon that is the way of the science of inference, along with the fact that the body is not free from motion or rest, and they cannot be combined, so half of its times are removed from motion and half from rest, and every possessor of a half is finite, because since they cannot be together in pre-eternity, the temporality of one of the two states is necessary, and they invalidate that it be temporally originated in pre-eternity; it becomes necessary in the other, and in that is the temporality of that which is not free from it. And also that every body is not free from permanent rest or permanent motion or both, and what it is upon from them is driven to it, compelled by it, and made for the benefits of others. And when that is the description of the substances of the world that are not described with life, it is established that they are temporally originated; for they are not upon what but upon their being subjugated, subdued, and used in the needs of others. And if that is established in the origin of itself, then likewise the substances and living beings that are in it and by it settle and benefit, while they are naturally disposed, and benefits are more deserving of that. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage starts by refuting an objection: someone might claim that the world's pre-eternity is not perceptible (hidden from sight) and therefore cannot be disproved. Maturidi responds that the world is known by sight (bi al-baṣar) and by proofs (adillah), and that the claim of pre-eternity based on occultation is weak. He then moves to a major proof from motion and rest. Every body is either in motion or at rest; these are mutually exclusive. Since a body alternates between motion and rest over time, neither motion nor rest can be everlasting. Each occupies half of the body's time, and anything divisible into halves is finite. Therefore, the body cannot be pre-eternal because that would require both motion and rest to coexist eternally, which is impossible. Hence, the body must be temporal. The author adds a second argument: every body is either permanently at rest, permanently in motion, or alternating. Even permanent motion or rest, if it is for the benefit of others, proves dependency and temporal origination. The substances (jawāhir) of the world are subjugated and used for the needs of others; this subjugation indicates they are created and not eternal. The passage concludes with the same pious phrase.

Key Terms
الحركة (al-ḥaraka)
السكون (al-sukūn)
الاستدلال (al-istidlāl)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that alternating motion and rest could be simultaneous if timeless, but the argument relies on real temporal alternation observed in bodies.
Correction: The alternation is temporal, not atemporal. The argument hinges on the fact that in time, motion and rest cannot coexist, so each must take a finite period.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that a body cannot be pre-eternal if it alternates between motion and rest?
A) Because motion and rest are both eternal
B) Because each occupies half the time, so the body's time is finite
C) Because the body would cease to exist
D) Because motion is prior to rest

Key Takeaway
The alternation of motion and rest in a body proves that it cannot be eternal, because each state occupies a finite portion of time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that your own body, which constantly alternates between motion and rest, cannot be eternal and will one day cease. Does this reality make you fear the moment when your breathing stops? How will you prepare today for that unavoidable end?
?
If every motion and rest of your body is finite and will be accounted for, are there actions (movements) or moments of stillness (rest) in your life that you are neglecting to use in obedience to Allah? Commit to changing one habit this week.
?
The proof shows that the world—including everything you own and love—is temporal. Is there any possession, relationship, or ambition that you have treated as if it will last forever? Pray for the strength to detach your heart from what will perish.

Further Proof: Subjugation and Dependency of Substances
Maturidi presents a second argument from subjugation of bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's second argument for the temporality of bodies, based on their subjugation and use for the needs of others.

Core Idea
What is subjugated for the benefit of others cannot be self-sufficient and eternal.

After establishing the temporal nature of bodies through motion and rest alternation, Maturidi presents a complementary argument: every body is either permanently at rest, permanently in motion, or alternating, and its state is not self-determined but driven to it. The substances (jawāhir) of the world are subjugated and used for the needs of others, indicating that they are created and dependent. This lesson explores that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the second argument
Read from 'وأيضا أن كل جسم لا يخلو عن سكون دائم' to the end. Note the different focus.
The passage also mentions living beings, but the core is about substances.
2
Identify the classification
The argument classifies bodies into three states: permanent rest, permanent motion, or alternating. For each, the state is imposed (not chosen).
3
Connect subjugation to temporality
Maturidi argues that because substances are subjugated and used for others' benefits, they cannot be eternal; they must be temporal creations.
The logic: dependency implies originated.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends with a statement about living beings being subjugated as well, reinforcing the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويلزم أيضا احتمال الابتداء ، وليس لقول من يقول : يغيب عن الأبصار ولا يعنى معنى ، لما علم العالم بالبصر لا بالدلائل ، وبه يُدعى القدم ، فقد مع ما أنا بينا من وهنه ، ولا فرق بين حياة يفنى وبين ذاته ، ولا زال ذلك قوه إلا بالله وعلى ذلك طريق علم الاستدلال ، مع ما أنه لا يخلو الجسم من حركة أو سكون ، وليس لها الإجتماع ، فيزول من جملة أوقاته نصف الحركة ونصف السكون، وكل ذى نصف متناه ، على أنها إذ لا يجتمعان في القدم لزم حدث أحد الوجهين ، ويبطلانه أن / يكون محدثا فى الأزل لزم فى الآخر ، وفي ذلك حدث ما لا يخلو عنه. وأيضا أن كل جسم لا يخلو عن سكون دائم أو حركة دائمة أو هما وما هو عليه منهما مدفوع إليه مسخر به ومجعول لمنافع غيره ، وإذا كان ذلك وصف جواهر العالم التى لا توصف بالحياة ثبت أنها محدثة ؛ إذ هي لا على ما ولكن على تسخيرها وتذليلها واستعمالها فى حوائج غيرها . وإذا ثبت ذلك في أصل هنى بنفسها فكذلك الجواهر والأحياء الذين هم فيها وبها تقر وننتفع وهم مجبولون والمنافع أحق بذلك ، والله الموفق
And also necessary is the possibility of beginning, and not for the saying of one who says: it is hidden from sight and has no meaning, because the world is known by sight, not by proofs, and by that pre-eternity is claimed – it has indeed, along with what we have shown of its weakness, no difference between a life that perishes and its essence, and that state of its strength only through God. And also that every body is not free from permanent rest or permanent motion or both, and what it is upon from them is driven to it, compelled by it, and made for the benefits of others. And when that is the description of the substances of the world that are not described with life, it is established that they are temporally originated; for they are not upon what but upon their being subjugated, subdued, and used in the needs of others. And if that is established in the origin of itself, then likewise the substances and living beings that are in it and by it settle and benefit, while they are naturally disposed, and benefits are more deserving of that. Commentary
This passage starts by refuting an objection: someone might claim that the world's pre-eternity is not perceptible (hidden from sight) and therefore cannot be disproved. Maturidi responds that the world is known by sight (bi al-baṣar) and by proofs (adillah), and that the claim of pre-eternity based on occultation is weak. Correction: Even if a body's state were permanent, the fact that it is compelled and used for others indicates it is not autonomous, hence it must be created.

Proof from Succession of Opposites
Maturidi enumerates opposite states and deduces temporality from their succession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the constant succession of opposite states in the world proves its temporality and refutes pre-eternity.

Core Idea
Succession of opposites implies temporality because opposites cannot coexist simultaneously.

Imam Maturidi now offers another compelling argument based on our direct experience of the world. We observe that the world constantly alternates between opposite states such as motion and rest, conjunction and separation. Since these opposites cannot exist together, they must succeed each other in time. This succession, as Maturidi explains, is a clear sign that the world is temporally originated (hadith), not eternal.

Guided Path
1
List the opposites mentioned
Read the beginning of the passage and identify the pairs of opposite states that Maturidi says characterize the world. Notice the range from physical (motion/rest) to moral (good/evil).
These opposites are observed by sense and reason.
2
Understand the logical principle
Maturidi states that it is logically impossible for two opposites to coexist simultaneously. If the world were eternal, all its states would have to coexist, but they cannot. Therefore, they must occur one after another.
This is the core of the argument: succession (taʿāqub) implies temporality.
3
Conclude temporality
From the succession of opposites, Maturidi deduces that the world must be temporal (hadith). He then notes that all temporal events are subsumed under existence after non-existence, and the world is not free from such events nor does it precede them.
The conclusion is that anyone who denies the temporality of the world is refuted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودليل آخر : أن العالم لا يخلو من أن يكون قديما على ما عليه أحواله من اجتماع وتفرق ، وحركة وسكون ، وخبيث وطيب ، وحسن وقبيح ، وزيادة ونقصان ، وهن حوادث بالحس والعقل ؛ إذ لا يجوز اجتماع الضدين ، فثبت التعاقب ، وفيه الحدث. وجميع الحوادث تحت الكون بعد أن لم تكن ما لا يخلو عنها ولا يسبقها ، أو كان إنشاء عن أصل لا بهذه الصفة أو انتقل إليها باعتراضها فيه ، فإن كان ذلك ثبت أن هذا العالم حانث ، وبطل قول من ينكر الحدوث ، وإن كان غير هذا فإن كان الأول هو المنشئ له فهو قولنا هو البارى وسموه هيولى ، وإن كان على الإنتقال إليه فذهب الأول وصار هذا غيره ، فهذا محدث بما لم يكن هو الأول ، والأول عندث بما هلك لما انتقل إلى الثانى ، ما لا يكون شيء من شيء من أن يكون مستجنا فيه فيظهر ، أو محدثا فيه فيتولد ويخرج ، أو يتلف الأول فيكون الثانى . فالأول كالولد والشيء الموضوع في الوعاء ، ومحال كون أضعاف ما فيه فما هو فيه ؛ لذلك يبطل القول أن يكون الإنسان من النطفة ، والشجر فى الحب ، وعلى ذلك من يقول بالبروز ما كان فى ذلك ايجاب حدث ذاته ، لأن القبوة عليه غيره إذ هو بالقوة ، مع وجد بالفعل لا بالقوة ، أو تلف الأول نحو النطفة ثم النسمة ونحو ذلك فيصير الأول مالكا حتى لا يبقى له الأثر ، والثانى حادثا حتى لم يبق من الأول فيه أثر . وفى ذلك حدث الأول والثانى
And another proof: that the world is not free from being pre-eternal upon what its states are of conjunction and separation, motion and rest, evil and good, beautiful and ugly, increase and decrease – and these are temporally originated by sense and intellect, for the conjunction of two opposites is not permissible; thus succession (al-taʿāqub) is established, and in it is temporality. And all temporal events are under existence after not having been, that which the world is not free from nor precedes them; or it was originated from an original not in this description, or transferred to it by their intervening in it. If that is the case, then it is established that this world is temporal, and the statement of one who denies temporality is invalid. And if it is other than this, then if the first is the originator of it, it is our saying: He is the Creator; and they call it hayula (matter). And if it is upon the transfer to it, then the first has gone and this has become other than it; so this is temporally originated because it was not the first, and the first is temporally originated because it perished when it transferred to the second. It is not possible for something to come from something except by being hidden within it and then appearing, or being temporally originated within it and then generated and emerging, or the first perishes and the second becomes. So the first is like the child and the thing placed in a container, and it is impossible for something to become many times what is in it; therefore the statement that a human comes from a sperm, and a tree from a seed, is invalid; and likewise one who says by manifestation – that does not necessitate the temporality of its essence, because the potentiality is from other than it, since it is in potentiality, while it is found in actuality not in potentiality; or the first perishes like the sperm then the soul, and so forth, so the first becomes non-existent until no trace remains, and the second becomes temporal until no trace of the first remains in it. And in that is the temporality of both the first and the second.
Source pages p. 612

Commentary
This passage is a self-contained argument for the temporality of the world from the constant succession of opposite states, followed by a refutation of those who claim the world originated from a pre-eternal principle (hayula). First, the world is characterized by opposites (conjunction/separation, motion/rest, etc.) that cannot coexist simultaneously; they must succeed each other. This succession (taʿāqub) implies temporality because each state comes after not existing. If the world were pre-eternal, it would have to have all its states simultaneously, which is impossible. Then Maturidi considers alternative theories: either the world was created from nothing (the correct view), or it was created from an eternal substrate (hayula), or it transferred from one state to another. He argues that if it was created from an eternal substrate, that substrate would have to be the Creator (which is false) or the first state perishes and the second arises, implying both are temporal. He uses examples like a child coming from a parent or a seed growing into a tree to illustrate that the latent potentiality cannot produce a new essence without the first perishing. The conclusion is that both the original matter and the resulting world are temporal, disproving the eternity of matter.

Key Terms
التعاقب (al-taʿāqub)
الضدان (al-ḍiddān)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key reason why Maturidi concludes that the world must be temporal?
A) The world is too complex to be eternal
B) Succession of opposites is impossible if the world were eternal
C) The world has a beginning in time by revelation
D) Opposites can coexist eternally

Key Takeaway
The constant succession of opposite states in the world proves its temporality and refutes the claim of pre-eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You live in a world of constant change—your body, your thoughts, your circumstances all shift. If everything around you is temporal, what are you relying on that will last? Are you anchoring your hope in something that does not change?
?
Maturidi argues that opposites cannot coexist in the same subject. Are there contradictory beliefs or desires within you—love of this world and love of Allah, fear of people and fear of Allah—that you try to hold simultaneously? How does this proof challenge you to resolve them?
?
The world is never free from succession; every moment is a new creation. Does this truth make you feel more aware of Allah's constant act of sustaining the universe? How does that awareness change the way you live this next hour?

Refutation of Eternal Matter (Hayula)
Maturidi refutes the idea of eternal matter and shows its temporality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in an eternal prime matter (hayula) from which the world was created is rationally false and leads to the temporality of both matter and the world.

Core Idea
Even if matter were eternal, its transformation into the world proves its temporality.

After establishing the temporality of the world, Imam Maturidi now turns to refute alternative theories that attempt to salvage some form of eternity. Specifically, he takes on the claim that the world was created from a pre-eternal substance (hayula) or through a transfer of states. By analyzing these possibilities, he demonstrates that they all entail that both the original substrate and the resulting world are temporal, leaving no room for any eternal entity besides Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two alternative theories
Maturidi considers two possibilities: (1) the world was originated from an original principle (hayula) that is not like the world, or (2) the world transferred from one state to another. Understand these two scenarios.
These are attempts to explain creation without a direct creation ex nihilo.
2
Analyze the argument against hayula
If the world came from hayula, then either hayula itself is the Creator (false) or it changes into the world. If it changes, then it is temporal because it was not the world and then becomes it.
Maturidi uses examples like a child from a parent or a tree from a seed to illustrate hidden potential.
3
Understand the argument against transfer
If the world is a result of transfer from a previous state, then the first state perishes and the second arises, making both temporal. Nothing can come from something without the first perishing or latent potential being actualized.
This refutes the idea of eternal matter underlying change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودليل آخر : أن العالم لا يخلو من أن يكون قديما على ما عليه أحواله من اجتماع وتفرق ، وحركة وسكون ، وخبيث وطيب ، وحسن وقبيح ، وزيادة ونقصان ، وهن حوادث بالحس والعقل ؛ إذ لا يجوز اجتماع الضدين ، فثبت التعاقب ، وفيه الحدث. وجميع الحوادث تحت الكون بعد أن لم تكن ما لا يخلو عنها ولا يسبقها ، أو كان إنشاء عن أصل لا بهذه الصفة أو انتقل إليها باعتراضها فيه ، فإن كان ذلك ثبت أن هذا العالم حانث ، وبطل قول من ينكر الحدوث ، وإن كان غير هذا فإن كان الأول هو المنشئ له فهو قولنا هو البارى وسموه هيولى ، وإن كان على الإنتقال إليه فذهب الأول وصار هذا غيره ، فهذا محدث بما لم يكن هو الأول ، والأول عندث بما هلك لما انتقل إلى الثانى ، ما لا يكون شيء من شيء من أن يكون مستجنا فيه فيظهر ، أو محدثا فيه فيتولد ويخرج ، أو يتلف الأول فيكون الثانى . فالأول كالولد والشيء الموضوع في الوعاء ، ومحال كون أضعاف ما فيه فما هو فيه ؛ لذلك يبطل القول أن يكون الإنسان من النطفة ، والشجر فى الحب ، وعلى ذلك من يقول بالبروز ما كان فى ذلك ايجاب حدث ذاته ، لأن القبوة عليه غيره إذ هو بالقوة ، مع وجد بالفعل لا بالقوة ، أو تلف الأول نحو النطفة ثم النسمة ونحو ذلك فيصير الأول مالكا حتى لا يبقى له الأثر ، والثانى حادثا حتى لم يبق من الأول فيه أثر . وفى ذلك حدث الأول والثانى
And another proof: that the world is not free from being pre-eternal upon what its states are of conjunction and separation, motion and rest, evil and good, beautiful and ugly, increase and decrease – and these are temporally originated by sense and intellect, for the conjunction of two opposites is not permissible; thus succession (al-taʿāqub) is established, and in it is temporality. And all temporal events are under existence after not having been, that which the world is not free from nor precedes them; or it was originated from an original not in this description, or transferred to it by their intervening in it. If that is the case, then it is established that this world is temporal, and the statement of one who denies temporality is invalid. And if it is other than this, then if the first is the originator of it, it is our saying: He is the Creator; and they call it hayula (matter). And if it is upon the transfer to it, then the first has gone and this has become other than it; so this is temporally originated because it was not the first, and the first is temporally originated because it perished when it transferred to the second. It is not possible for something to come from something except by being hidden within it and then appearing, or being temporally originated within it and then generated and emerging, or the first perishes and the second becomes. So the first is like the child and the thing placed in a container, and it is impossible for something to become many times what is in it; therefore the statement that a human comes from a sperm, and a tree from a seed, is invalid; and likewise one who says by manifestation – that does not necessitate the temporality of its essence, because the potentiality is from other than it, since it is in potentiality, while it is found in actuality not in potentiality; or the first perishes like the sperm then the soul, and so forth, so the first becomes non-existent until no trace remains, and the second becomes temporal until no trace of the first remains in it. And in that is the temporality of both the first and the second.
Source pages p. 612

Commentary
This passage is a self-contained argument for the temporality of the world from the constant succession of opposite states, followed by a refutation of those who claim the world originated from a pre-eternal principle (hayula). First, the world is characterized by opposites (conjunction/separation, motion/rest, etc.) that cannot coexist simultaneously; they must succeed each other. This succession (taʿāqub) implies temporality because each state comes after not existing. If the world were pre-eternal, it would have to have all its states simultaneously, which is impossible. Then Maturidi considers alternative theories: either the world was created from nothing (the correct view), or it was created from an eternal substrate (hayula), or it transferred from one state to another. He argues that if it was created from an eternal substrate, that substrate would have to be the Creator (which is false) or the first state perishes and the second arises, implying both are temporal. He uses examples like a child coming from a parent or a seed growing into a tree to illustrate that the latent potentiality cannot produce a new essence without the first perishing. The conclusion is that both the original matter and the resulting world are temporal, disproving the eternity of matter.

Key Terms
الهيولى (al-hayula)
القوة (al-quwwa)
الفعل (al-fiʿl)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The world could have been created from an eternally existing matter (hayula) without that matter itself being temporal.
Correction: Maturidi shows that any matter that undergoes change to produce the world must itself be temporal, because it either perishes or holds potentiality that becomes actuality, both of which imply temporality.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the consequence if the world originates from a transfer from a previous state?
A) The first state remains eternal
B) Both the first and second states are temporal
C) Only the second state is temporal
D) The first state is the Creator

Key Takeaway
No eternal matter can explain the world's existence; any alleged pre-eternal substrate must itself be temporal, affirming that only Allah is pre-eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You naturally rely on created things – your health, wealth, relationships – as if they were permanent foundations. But this lesson shows that every created thing, even if it were imagined as eternal matter, is temporal and perishes. Where in your life have you anchored your sense of security in something that will inevitably vanish? Will you now transfer that anchor solely to the Eternal Creator, even if it costs you the illusion of control?
?
If you truly believe that only Allah is pre-eternal, then what right do you have to fear the loss of anything other than Him? Your fear of losing health, status, or people reveals that you treat them as if they were eternal. Maturidi’s argument levels that lie. Today, what is one created thing you are holding onto as if it could never leave you? Write it down, and then pray to Allah to remove its grip from your heart.
?
This passage exposes the false hope of grounding the world in an eternal substrate. But you might still have a 'substrate' in your own life – a person, a plan, a possession – that you treat as the unchanging foundation. If Allah took that away, would your faith collapse? What would it take for you to make Allah alone your ground, the One who does not pass away? Commit to one concrete action this week that loosens your grip on that temporal support.

The Proof from Succession of Opposites
Maturidi presents the core proof from succession of opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the observable succession of opposite attributes in the world to prove its temporal origination.

Core Idea
The alternation of opposites in the world proves it is not eternal.

Maturidi presents a concise proof based on a simple observation: the world's attributes—like motion and rest, composition and separation—are constantly changing. Since opposites cannot coexist, their succession shows that the world is temporally originated. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's rhythm come through.
2
Identify the opposites listed
Maturidi lists pairs of opposite attributes: gathering/separation, motion/rest, bad/good, beautiful/foul, increase/decrease. Notice that these are observable and change over time.
These are called 'aʿrāḍ' (accidents) in kalam.
3
Understand why succession proves temporality
Because opposites cannot coexist in the same subject at the same time, their alternation implies change. Change is a sign of being temporally originated (ḥadath). Ask yourself: could an eternal being have changing attributes?
This is a foundational argument in Ashʿarī and Māturīdī kalām.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودليل آخر : أن العالم لا يخلو من أن يكون قديما على ما عليه أحواله من اجتماع وتفرق ، وحركة وسكون ، وخبيث وطيب ، وحسن رقيح ، وزيادة ونقصان ، وهن حوادث بالحس والعقل ; إذ لا يجوز اجتماع الضدين ، فثبت التعاقب ، وفيه الحدث. وجميع الحوادث تحت الكون بعد أن لم تكن ما لا يخلو عنها ولا يسبقها ، أو كان إنشاء عن أصل لا بهذه الصفة أو انتقل إليها باعتراضها فيه ، فإن كان ذلك ثبت أن هذا العالم حانث ، وبطل قول من ينكر [الحدوث ، وإن كان غير هذا فإن كان الأول هو المنشئ له فهو قولنا هو البارى وسموه هيولى ، وإن كان على الإنتقال إليه فذهب الأول وصار هذا غيره ، فهذا محدث بما لم يكن هو الأول ، والأول عندث بما هلك لما انتقل إلى الثانى ، ما لا يكون شيء من شيء من أن يكون مستجنا فيه فيظهر ، أو محدثا فيه فيتولد ويخرج ، أو يتلف الأول فيكون الثانى . فالأول كالولد / والشيء الموضوع في الوعاء ، ومحال كون أضعاف ما فيه فما هو فيه ; لذلك يبطل القول ١٠ يكون الإنسان من النطفة ، والشجر فى الحب ، وعلى ذلك من يقول بالبروز ما كان فى ذلك ايجاب حدث ذاته ، لأن القبوة عليه غيره إذ هو بالقوة ، مع وجد بالفعل لا بالقوة ، أو تلف الأول نحو النطفة ثم النسمة ونحو ذلك فيصير الأول مالكا حتى لا يبقى له الأثر ، والثانى حادثا حتى لم يبق من الأول فيه أثر . وفى ذلك حدث الأول والثانى .
Another proof: The world cannot but be either eternal as it is in its states of gathering and separation, motion and rest, bad and good, beautiful and foul, increase and decrease – and these are temporally originated (hawādith) by sense and reason, because the union of opposites is impossible. Thus succession is established, and in it is temporality (ḥadath). And all temporally originated things are under existence after non-existence, which the world cannot be free of and which do not precede it, or it was created from an origin not of this description, or it transferred to it by their occurring in it. If that is the case, then this world is temporal (ḥānith), and the statement of the one who denies [temporality] is false. And if it is otherwise, then if the first (origin) is the creator of it, it is our statement that it is the Creator (al-Bārī) – and they call it Hyle (hayūlā). And if it is by transfer to it, then the first perishes and this becomes other than it, so this is originated (muḥdath) because it was not the first, and the first is temporal because it perished when it transferred to the second. Nothing comes from anything either by being concealed in it then appearing, or being originated in it then generated and emerging, or the first perishing then the second coming. So the first is like the child and the object placed in a container, and it is impossible for multiples of what is in it to be contained in it. Therefore the statement that man comes from a drop, and the tree from a seed, and likewise the one who says by emergence (al-burūz) that which necessitates the temporality of its essence, because the potential (al-quwwa) of it is other than it, since it is in potentiality not actuality, or the perishing of the first like the drop then the soul, etc., so the first becomes non-existent leaving no trace, and the second becomes originated having no trace of the first in it. And in that is the temporality of the first and the second.
Source pages p. 612

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalīl) for the temporal origination (ḥudūth) of the world, based on the observation that the world's attributes (such as motion, rest, composition, separation, etc.) are subject to change and succession. Since opposites cannot coexist, the fact that these attributes alternate indicates that the world is not eternal but originated. Maturidi then refutes alternative explanations: that the world might have been derived from an eternal origin without these changing attributes, or that it might have transferred from one state to another. He argues that in all cases, the first state perishes and the second is new, thus both are temporal. He concludes that any theory of generation (e.g., man from sperm) ultimately implies temporality of both the source and the product.

Key Terms
دليل
حدوث
حوادث
الضدين
التعاقب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the argument assumes the attributes themselves are eternal; rather, it is their changeability that proves temporality.
Correction: Maturidi argues from the fact that attributes change, not from their permanence.

Checkpoint
What does the succession of opposites in the world demonstrate according to Maturidi?
A) That the world is eternal
B) That the world is temporally originated
C) That the world is a body
D) That the world has no beginning

Key Takeaway
The observable alternation of opposite attributes in the world provides a rational proof that the world is temporally originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You observe change every day—your moods, your surroundings, your relationships. This proof shows that such alternation cannot be eternal. If the world is constantly changing, what does that say about your attachment to things that are fleeting? Will you hold on to them or seek the Eternal?
?
The proof hinges on the impossibility of opposites coexisting. Yet in your own heart, you may try to hold contradictory desires—like loving both this world and the next without prioritizing. What one contradiction do you need to resolve today to align with the truth of tawheed?
?
Al-Maturidi lists pairs like 'good and bad' as opposites that alternate. Think of a recent time you experienced a shift from good to bad or vice versa. Did that moment remind you that this world is not your final home? How can you use that memory to strengthen your reliance on Allah?

Refuting Alternative Origins
Maturidi refutes alternative explanations for the world's origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the ideas that the world could be eternal via an origin or transfer, and his conclusion that all alternatives imply temporality.

Core Idea
Every theory of the world's origin leads to temporality of both source and product.

After establishing the basic proof, Maturidi anticipates objections: perhaps the world's changing attributes arise from an eternal origin, or through a transfer of states. He systematically shows that these alternatives also entail temporality. This lesson examines his refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully; it is dense. Then read the literal translation.
Note the technical terms: 'هيولى' (Hyle), 'بروز' (emergence), 'قوة' (potential).
2
Identify the three alternatives considered
Maturidi considers: (1) the world is created from an origin not of this description, (2) it transferred to its current state, (3) something emerges from something else. Find these in the text.
3
Analyze the refutation of each alternative
For each alternative, Maturidi argues that it either implies a creator (which is Allah) or results in the perishing of the first state and the origination of the second, hence both are temporal.
The point is to show that no alternative avoids temporality.
4
Understand the analogies (child, container, drop, seed)
Maturidi uses analogies to illustrate that nothing comes from something without either being concealed, generated, or the first perishing. The analogies show the impossibility of pre-existence in the source.
These analogies refute preformationist theories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودليل آخر : أن العالم لا يخلو من أن يكون قديما على ما عليه أحواله من اجتماع وتفرق ، وحركة وسكون ، وخبيث وطيب ، وحسن رقيح ، وزيادة ونقصان ، وهن حوادث بالحس والعقل ; إذ لا يجوز اجتماع الضدين ، فثبت التعاقب ، وفيه الحدث. وجميع الحوادث تحت الكون بعد أن لم تكن ما لا يخلو عنها ولا يسبقها ، أو كان إنشاء عن أصل لا بهذه الصفة أو انتقل إليها باعتراضها فيه ، فإن كان ذلك ثبت أن هذا العالم حانث ، وبطل قول من ينكر [الحدوث ، وإن كان غير هذا فإن كان الأول هو المنشئ له فهو قولنا هو البارى وسموه هيولى ، وإن كان على الإنتقال إليه فذهب الأول وصار هذا غيره ، فهذا محدث بما لم يكن هو الأول ، والأول عندث بما هلك لما انتقل إلى الثانى ، ما لا يكون شيء من شيء من أن يكون مستجنا فيه فيظهر ، أو محدثا فيه فيتولد ويخرج ، أو يتلف الأول فيكون الثانى . فالأول كالولد / والشيء الموضوع في الوعاء ، ومحال كون أضعاف ما فيه فما هو فيه ; لذلك يبطل القول ١٠ يكون الإنسان من النطفة ، والشجر فى الحب ، وعلى ذلك من يقول بالبروز ما كان فى ذلك ايجاب حدث ذاته ، لأن القبوة عليه غيره إذ هو بالقوة ، مع وجد بالفعل لا بالقوة ، أو تلف الأول نحو النطفة ثم النسمة ونحو ذلك فيصير الأول مالكا حتى لا يبقى له الأثر ، والثانى حادثا حتى لم يبق من الأول فيه أثر . وفى ذلك حدث الأول والثانى .
Another proof: The world cannot but be either eternal as it is in its states of gathering and separation, motion and rest, bad and good, beautiful and foul, increase and decrease – and these are temporally originated (hawādith) by sense and reason, because the union of opposites is impossible. Thus succession is established, and in it is temporality (ḥadath). And all temporally originated things are under existence after non-existence, which the world cannot be free of and which do not precede it, or it was created from an origin not of this description, or it transferred to it by their occurring in it. If that is the case, then this world is temporal (ḥānith), and the statement of the one who denies [temporality] is false. And if it is otherwise, then if the first (origin) is the creator of it, it is our statement that it is the Creator (al-Bārī) – and they call it Hyle (hayūlā). And if it is by transfer to it, then the first perishes and this becomes other than it, so this is originated (muḥdath) because it was not the first, and the first is temporal because it perished when it transferred to the second. Nothing comes from anything either by being concealed in it then appearing, or being originated in it then generated and emerging, or the first perishing then the second coming. So the first is like the child and the object placed in a container, and it is impossible for multiples of what is in it to be contained in it. Therefore the statement that man comes from a drop, and the tree from a seed, and likewise the one who says by emergence (al-burūz) that which necessitates the temporality of its essence, because the potential (al-quwwa) of it is other than it, since it is in potentiality not actuality, or the perishing of the first like the drop then the soul, etc., so the first becomes non-existent leaving no trace, and the second becomes originated having no trace of the first in it. And in that is the temporality of the first and the second.

Commentary

Since opposites cannot coexist, the fact that these attributes alternate indicates that the world is not eternal but originated. He argues that in all cases, the first state perishes and the second is new, thus both are temporal. He concludes that any theory of generation (e.g., man from sperm) ultimately implies temporality of both the source and the product.

Correction: Maturidi argues that the sperm perishes and the human is a new creation; both are temporal.

Maturidi shows that any theory of origination—whether from an eternal origin, transfer, or emergence—ultimately leads to the temporality of both the source and the product.

?
If everything besides Allah is temporal and dependent on Him for existence at every moment, what does that mean for the things you worry about? Are you treating your problems as independent realities? This week, commit to reminding yourself that everything besides Allah is a passing temporal event. How will you do that?
?
Maturidi argues that the product does not pre-exist in the source in actuality. How does this challenge your own view of personal growth or change? Are you trying to bring out something already inside you, or are you relying on Allah to create new realities? What change do you need to ask Allah to create in you today?
?
The passage refutes the idea that the world is eternal. Yet sometimes we live as if our routines and habits are permanent. What is one area of your life where you have acted as if it will never change? How will you realign your heart with the reality that only Allah is eternal?

beginner
