Proof of the Creator's Oneness: Scripture and Numerical Evidence
Maturidi begins the proof that the creator is one with scriptural and numerical arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's scriptural and rational arguments for the oneness of the Creator, particularly his use of a numerical argument to refute polytheism.

Core Idea
Maturidi proves divine unity by showing that multiplicity leads to absurd infinities.

Maturidi begins his Kitab al-Tawhid by establishing the oneness of the Creator through multiple proofs. In this passage, he outlines three sources of evidence—scripture, reason, and the witness of creation—and then elaborates on the scriptural and numerical arguments. This lesson unpacks his reasoning, showing how even the language of polytheists points to unity and how arithmetic logic defeats multiplicity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation to get the flow of Maturidi's argument.
2
Identify the three sources of evidence
Maturidi opens by listing three proofs: scripture (as-sam‘), reason (al-‘aql), and the witness of the world (shahādat al-‘ālam). Note that he only elaborates on scripture and a rational numerical argument.
3
Understand the scriptural argument
Maturidi argues that even polytheists agree on the term 'one' (al-wāḥid) in a sense of uniqueness and greatness, not just numerical beginning. This shows a common ground that the creator is one.
4
Grasp the numerical argument
Maturidi presents a reductio ad absurdum: if there were multiple creators, each producing one thing, the world would be infinite, which is impossible. Also, any claimed number can be increased or decreased, so the claim of multiple creators has no basis.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that the assertion of more than one creator is invalid. Reflect on how this argument fits into the broader Islamic theological defense of tawḥīd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : والدلالة أن مُحدث العالم واحد لا أكثر السمع والعقل وشهادة العالم بالخلقة. فأما السمع فهو اتفاق القول، على اختلافهم على الواحد، إذ من يقول بالأكثر يقول به على أن الواحد اسم لابتداء العدد واسم للعظمة والسلطان والرفعة والفضل، كما يقال: فلان واحد الزمان ومنقطع القرين في الرفعة والفضل والجلال، وما جاوز ذلك لا يحتمل غير العدد، والأعداد لا من حيث العدد، وفي تحقيق ما يُعد يخرج عن النهاية العدد، فيجب أن يكون العالم غير متناه؛ إذ لو كان من كل منهم شيء واحد، فيخرج الجملة عن التناهي بخروج المحدثين، وذلك بعيد. ثم ما من عدد يشار إليه إلا نهاية لنا وأمكن من الدعوى أن يُزادَ عليه ويُنقص منه، فلم يجب القول بشيء لا حقيقة لذلك بحق العدد - لا يشارك فيه غيره؛ لذلك بطل القول به، وبالله التوفيق.
Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: The evidence that the maker of the world is one, not more, is [from] scripture (as-sam‘), reason (al-‘aql), and the witness of the world by creation. As for scripture: it is the agreement of statements, despite their differences, upon the one. For whoever says there are more says so [only] because 'one' is a name for the beginning of number and a name for greatness, authority, elevation, and excellence, just as it is said: 'So-and-so is the one of the age and the peerless in elevation, excellence, and majesty.' What goes beyond that does not admit [anything] other than number. And numbers—not by virtue of number—and in the realization of what is counted, [the count] leaves the limit of number. Therefore the world must be infinite, for if from each of them there were one thing, the whole would exit from finitude by the exiting of the originated things, and that is far[-fetched]. Then, there is no number pointed to except that we have an end, and it is possible for the claim to be increased upon it and decreased from it. So the assertion of something that has no reality in terms of the right of number—not shared by anything else—is not necessary; therefore the assertion of it is invalid. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 618

Commentary
This passage presents the initial proof for the oneness of the creator (muhdith al-‘alam). Maturidi begins by stating that the evidence comes from three sources: scripture (as-sam‘), reason (al-‘aql), and the witness of the world through its creation (shahādat al-‘ālam bi’l-khalq). He first expounds the scriptural evidence. He notes that there is a consensus (ittifāq al-qawl) among all groups, despite their differences, on the term 'one' (al-wāḥid). Even those who assert multiple gods use the word 'one' in the sense of the beginning of number, but also in the sense of greatness, authority, and excellence, as when someone is called 'the one of the age' meaning peerless. Beyond the beginning of number, it does not apply. He then makes a rational argument about numbers: if we consider the actual counted objects, the count would go beyond any finite limit, implying that the world would be infinite—an absurd consequence. Moreover, any claimed number can be increased or decreased, so asserting a specific plurality has no basis in the right of number (ḥaqq al-‘adad) that is uniquely possessed. Therefore the claim of multiple creators is invalid.

Key Terms
محدث العالم (muhdith al-‘ālam)
السمع (as-sam‘)
العقل (al-‘aql)
الواحد (al-wāḥid)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the term 'one' (wāḥid) only refers to the number one, missing its connotation of uniqueness and greatness.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that 'one' is also used to denote greatness, authority, and peerlessness, as in 'the one of the age'. This dual meaning allows even polytheists to affirm a sense of oneness for their chief god.

Checkpoint
What is the first source of evidence Maturidi mentions for the oneness of the creator?
A) Reason
B) Scripture
C) The witness of the world
D) Consensus

Key Takeaway
Maturidi argues that the concept of multiple creators leads to logical absurdity, affirming the oneness of the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that even polytheists use the word 'one' to describe greatness, yet they attach partners to God. In your own life, do you ever verbally affirm God's oneness while subtly trusting in other 'ones'—like your intelligence, wealth, or reputation—as the real sources of your security? How would Maturidi's argument expose this inconsistency, and what step will you take today to align your heart's reliance with your tongue's confession?
?
Maturidi argues that any claimed number of creators can be increased or decreased, making any specific number arbitrary. Is there an area in your faith where you have added a 'partner'—not in worship, but in seeking meaning, comfort, or control (like a relationship, career, or ideology)? This arbitrariness shows the absurdity of dividing your ultimate allegiance. What concrete action can you take this week to remove that false 'partner' from the throne of your heart?
?
The proof begins by stating that reason and scripture agree on God's oneness. Are there moments when you feel a tension between what your intellect accepts and what revelation commands? This passage challenges you to examine that tension: is it a genuine contradiction or a failure of your understanding? What question about your faith are you afraid to honestly submit to both reason and revelation, and what would it cost you to seek that harmony?

The Futility of False Claims and the Prophetic Proof
Maturidi dismisses false claims to divinity and argues that prophetic signs prove the true God is One.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the absence of evidence for other gods and the unique signs of prophets to establish tawhid.

Core Idea
No false god ever produced evidence; the prophets' undeniable signs prove the One, All-Subduing God.

Maturidi opens by observing that no rival deity has ever presented a genuine claim with proof. He then points to the miracles of the prophets: if another god existed, that partner would have stopped them—yet no such prevention occurred. This establishes the true God as al-Wāḥid al-Qahhār, the One who subdues all obstinacy.

Guided Path
1
Observe the opening claim
Notice how Maturidi states that no other god has brought forward any evidence of divinity. This sets up the argument from absence.
2
Reflect on the prophetic signs
The messengers brought overpowering signs. If another god existed, he would have prevented these signs, as they undermine his claim. Since no prevention occurred, there is no partner.
This is an argument from what would have been visible.
3
Understand the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that the true God is the One who subdues all pretenders. The phrase 'لا قوة إلا بالله' emphasizes reliance on Allah's power.
This verse-like phrase closes the section.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد، فإنه لم يذكر عن غير الإله الذي يعرفه أهل التوحيد دعوى الإلهية والإشارة إلى أثر فعل منه يدل على ربوبيته، ولا وجد في شيء معنى أمكن إخراجه عن حمله، ولا بَعَثَ رُسلا بالآيات التى تقهر العقول ويبهر لها، فتثبت أن القول بذلك خيال ووسواس. وأيضا نجي الرسل بالآيات التى يضطر من شهدها أنها فعل من لو كان معه شريك ليمنعهم عن إظهارها؛ إذ بذلك إبطال ربوبيتهم وألوهيتهم، فإذ لم يوجد ولا معوا عن ذلك مع كثرة المكابرين والمعاندين ممن لو أحبوا وجود الإبدار لهم في إظهار أيامهم لوجدوا - فثبت أن ذلك إنما سليم للرسل؛ لما يكن الإله الحق والخالق للخلق غير الواحد القهار الذي قهر كل متعنت متعنت مكابر عن التمويه فضلا من التحقيق، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم دلالة العقل أنه لو كان أكثر من واحد ما احتمل وجود العالم إلا بالإصطلاح وفي ذلك فساد الربوبية. ومعنى آخر: أن كل شيء يُريد أحد ممن يُنسب إليه إثباته يريد الآخر نفيه، وما يريد أحدهما إيجاده يريد الآخر إعدامه، وكذلك في الإبقاء والإفناء، وفي ذلك تناقض وتناف، فدل الوجود على محدث العالم واحد تدبيره مع ما كان الأمر المعتاد بين الماوك بذل الوسع منهم في قهر أشكالهم ليكون الملك للقاهر، ومنع كل منهم غيره عن إنفاذ حكمه، وإظهار سلطانه ما استطاع، فإذ لم يكن - بل نفذ سلطان العزيز الحكيم - ثبت أنه الواحد. وهذا تأويل قوله: قُلْ لَوْ كَانَ مَعَهُ آلِهَةٌ كَمَا يَقُولُونَ إِذًا لابْتَغُوا إلى ذِي العَرْشِ سَبِيلاً، والأول على ما أودع قوله: لَوْ كَانَ فيهما آلِهَةً إِلَّا اللهُ لَفَسَدَنَا.
And moreover, he has not mentioned any claim to divinity from other than the God known to the people of tawhid, nor any indication of an effect of His act that indicates His lordship, nor has he found in anything a meaning that could be removed from His meaning, nor has he sent messengers with signs that overpower intellects and dazzle them, so it is established that the assertion of that is fantasy and whisper [of Satan]. And also, the messengers came with signs that compel whoever witnesses them [to know] that they are the act of one who, if He had a partner, would prevent them from manifesting them, for in that is the nullification of their lordship and divinity. Since it has not existed nor have they been prevented from that despite the abundance of the obstinate and the stubborn who, if they had loved the existence of the manifesting of their days, they would have found [it]—so it is established that that is only given to the messengers because the true God and Creator of creation is none other than the One, the Subduer, who has subdued every obstinate, obstinate, stubborn [person] from pretense, let alone reality. And there is no power except with God. Then the evidence of reason: that if there were more than one, the existence of the world would only be possible through agreement, and in that is the corruption of lordship. And another meaning: that everything that one wants to affirm, the other wants to negate; what one wants to bring into existence, the other wants to annihilate; similarly in preservation and annihilation—in that is contradiction and conflict. So existence indicates that the maker of the world is one in its management, along with what was the customary affair among kings: the exertion of their effort in subduing their likes so that kingship belongs to the subduer, and each prevents the other from executing his judgment and manifesting his authority as much as he can. Since that was not [the case]—rather, the authority of the Mighty, the Wise has been executed—it is established that He is the One. And this is the interpretation of His saying: 'Say: If there were with Him gods as they say, then they would seek a way to the Owner of the Throne' (Q17:42), and the first is according to what He included in His saying: 'If there were in them gods besides Allah, they would both have been corrupted' (Q21:22).
Source pages p. 619

Commentary
This passage continues the proof of tawhid with additional rational and scriptural arguments. Maturidi first notes that no one has genuinely claimed divinity with evidence; all false claims are baseless. The prophets brought undeniable signs that, if there were another god, that partner would have prevented them—proving that the true God is One and All-Subduing (al-wāḥid al-qahhār). Then he presents the rational proof (dalīl al-‘aql): if there were more than one god, the world could only exist through their mutual agreement (iṣṭilāḥ), which would imply corruption of lordship (fasād al-rubūbiyya). More precisely, one god would will something, another would will its opposite, leading to contradiction (tanāquḍ) and conflict (tanāfun). The actual order of existence shows a single management. He draws an analogy with kings who strive to dominate each other, but here there is no such conflict; the authority of Allah alone prevails. Finally, he cites two Quranic verses as support: Q17:42 and Q21:22, which show that multiple gods would seek to reach the Throne or would cause corruption.

Key Terms
الواحد القهار (al-wāḥid al-qahhār)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is simply 'absence of evidence is evidence of absence' and is weak.
Correction: Maturidi's argument is not a simple absence of evidence; it is based on the necessary implication that a rival god would have inevitably interfered with the prophets' signs to protect his own claim. Since no such interference occurred, it proves the impossibility of a second god.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Maturidi say that false claims of divinity are 'fantasy and whisper'?
A) Because they have no evidence from acts or messengers
B) Because they contradict the Quran
C) Because the claimants are liars
D) Because people do not accept them

Key Takeaway
The absence of evidence for other gods, combined with the undeniable signs of prophets that no rival prevented, establishes the true God as One and All-Subduing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What false 'gods' in your life—status, wealth, relationships, or yourself—have you never stopped to examine whether they have any real evidence of power or benefit? Will you test them today by the same standard Maturidi used?
?
The prophets' signs were so compelling that if any other god existed, he would have stopped them to protect his own claim. Has anything ever stopped you from surrendering to the truth of Islam—pride, fear, or love of this world? What is preventing you from submitting to the One who subdued all obstacles?
?
You have witnessed countless signs of Allah’s power and mercy. Yet, have you responded with the same obstinacy as those Maturidi mentions—seeing the evidence but refusing to change? Will you, right now, prostrate in gratitude and admit that none deserves worship but Him?

Rational Proof from Conflict and Quranic Support
Maturidi presents rational arguments for tawhid based on the impossibility of agreement and the necessity of conflict, then cites Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that multiple gods would lead to conflict and corruption, and how the Quran supports this.

Core Idea
If there were two gods, their wills would conflict, causing corruption; the world’s order proves a single God.

Maturidi now turns to pure rational argument. He argues that if there were more than one god, the world could only exist through their agreement—which implies dependence and corruption of divinity. More precisely, their wills would inevitably contradict each other, leading to conflict. He illustrates with the analogy of kings who strive to dominate. Finally, he cites two Quranic verses that reinforce this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the argument from agreement
Maturidi says that if there were multiple gods, the world's existence would require their mutual agreement, which implies imperfection in lordship.
This is because a perfect God would not need to consult or agree.
2
Analyze the argument from conflict
He then points out that one god would want something, the other would want its opposite—leading to contradiction and conflict, which is not observed.
This is a stronger argument because it does not assume cooperation.
3
Learn the king analogy
Kings tend to subdue each other to gain sole authority. If there were multiple gods, such conflict would be expected, but it is absent.
This analogy is based on observable human behavior.
4
Connect to Quranic evidence
Maturidi cites Q17:42 and Q21:22 to show that multiple gods would seek to overthrow the Throne or cause corruption.
The Quranic verses serve as scriptural confirmation of the rational argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد، فإنه لم يذكر عن غير الإله الذي يعرفه أهل التوحيد دعوى الإلهية والإشارة إلى أثر فعل منه يدل على ربوبيته، ولا وجد في شيء معنى أمكن إخراجه عن حمله، ولا بَعَثَ رُسلا بالآيات التى تقهر العقول ويبهر لها، فتثبت أن القول بذلك خيال ووسواس. وأيضا نجي الرسل بالآيات التى يضطر من شهدها أنها فعل من لو كان معه شريك ليمنعهم عن إظهارها؛ إذ بذلك إبطال ربوبيتهم وألوهيتهم، فإذ لم يوجد ولا معوا عن ذلك مع كثرة المكابرين والمعاندين ممن لو أحبوا وجود الإبدار لهم في إظهار أيامهم لوجدوا - فثبت أن ذلك إنما سليم للرسل؛ لما يكن الإله الحق والخالق للخلق غير الواحد القهار الذي قهر كل متعنت متعنت مكابر عن التمويه فضلا من التحقيق، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم دلالة العقل أنه لو كان أكثر من واحد ما احتمل وجود العالم إلا بالإصطلاح وفي ذلك فساد الربوبية. ومعنى آخر: أن كل شيء يُريد أحد ممن يُنسب إليه إثباته يريد الآخر نفيه، وما يريد أحدهما إيجاده يريد الآخر إعدامه، وكذلك في الإبقاء والإفناء، وفي ذلك تناقض وتناف، فدل الوجود على محدث العالم واحد تدبيره مع ما كان الأمر المعتاد بين الماوك بذل الوسع منهم في قهر أشكالهم ليكون الملك للقاهر، ومنع كل منهم غيره عن إنفاذ حكمه، وإظهار سلطانه ما استطاع، فإذ لم يكن - بل نفذ سلطان العزيز الحكيم - ثبت أنه الواحد. وهذا تأويل قوله: قُلْ لَوْ كَانَ مَعَهُ آلِهَةٌ كَمَا يَقُولُونَ إِذًا لابْتَغُوا إلى ذِي العَرْشِ سَبِيلاً، والأول على ما أودع قوله: لَوْ كَانَ فيهما آلِهَةً إِلَّا اللهُ لَفَسَدَنَا.
And moreover, he has not mentioned any claim to divinity from other than the God known to the people of tawhid, nor any indication of an effect of His act that indicates His lordship, nor has he found in anything a meaning that could be removed from His meaning, nor has he sent messengers with signs that overpower intellects and dazzle them, so it is established that the assertion of that is fantasy and whisper [of Satan]. And also, the messengers came with signs that compel whoever witnesses them [to know] that they are the act of one who, if He had a partner, would prevent them from manifesting them, for in that is the nullification of their lordship and divinity. Since it has not existed nor have they been prevented from that despite the abundance of the obstinate and the stubborn who, if they had loved the existence of the manifesting of their days, they would have found [it]—so it is established that that is only given to the messengers because the true God and Creator of creation is none other than the One, the Subduer, who has subdued every obstinate, obstinate, stubborn [person] from pretense, let alone reality. And there is no power except with God. Then the evidence of reason: that if there were more than one, the existence of the world would only be possible through agreement, and in that is the corruption of lordship. And another meaning: that everything that one wants to affirm, the other wants to negate; what one wants to bring into existence, the other wants to annihilate; similarly in preservation and annihilation—in that is contradiction and conflict. So existence indicates that the maker of the world is one in its management, along with what was the customary affair among kings: the exertion of their effort in subduing their likes so that kingship belongs to the subduer, and each prevents the other from executing his judgment and manifesting his authority as much as he can. Since that was not [the case]—rather, the authority of the Mighty, the Wise has been executed—it is established that He is the One. And this is the interpretation of His saying: 'Say: If there were with Him gods as they say, then they would seek a way to the Owner of the Throne' (Q17:42), and the first is according to what He included in His saying: 'If there were in them gods besides Allah, they would both have been corrupted' (Q21:22).
Source pages p. 619

Commentary
This passage continues the proof of tawhid with additional rational and scriptural arguments. Maturidi first notes that no one has genuinely claimed divinity with evidence; all false claims are baseless. The prophets brought undeniable signs that, if there were another god, that partner would have prevented them—proving that the true God is One and All-Subduing (al-wāḥid al-qahhār). Then he presents the rational proof (dalīl al-‘aql): if there were more than one god, the world could only exist through their mutual agreement (iṣṭilāḥ), which would imply corruption of lordship (fasād al-rubūbiyya). More precisely, one god would will something, another would will its opposite, leading to contradiction (tanāquḍ) and conflict (tanāfun). The actual order of existence shows a single management. He draws an analogy with kings who strive to dominate each other, but here there is no such conflict; the authority of Allah alone prevails. Finally, he cites two Quranic verses as support: Q17:42 and Q21:22, which show that multiple gods would seek to reach the Throne or would cause corruption.

Key Terms
دلالة العقل (dalīl al-‘aql)
فساد الربوبية (fasād al-rubūbiyya)
تناقض (tanāquḍ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument assumes that gods would have conflicting desires, which may not be true if they are perfectly harmonious.
Correction: Maturidi's argument is not based on assumption; it is a logical necessity that if there are two omnipotent beings, they would have independent wills, and if those wills ever differ, conflict arises. Harmony would require one to submit, which negates omnipotence.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's rational proof, what would happen if there were multiple gods?
A) They would cooperate perfectly
B) Their wills would conflict, leading to corruption
C) They would remain hidden
D) They would share power equally

Key Takeaway
The rational proof shows that multiple gods would necessarily conflict, and the observed order of the universe, along with Quranic verses, confirms that God is One.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life have you allowed conflicting 'gods'—such as status, comfort, or relationships—to compete with the absolute authority of Allah, leading to inner turmoil? How will you dethrone them today?
?
The rational proof shows that multiple gods would necessarily conflict, yet your own heart may harbor divided loyalties. What specific step will you take this week to realign your priorities under the sole authority of the One God?
?
If the corruption of lordship (fasād al-rubūbiyya) stems from dependence on others, examine your heart: are you relying on creation rather than the Creator for your sense of security and worth? What concrete act of tawakkul (trust in Allah) can you practice today to affirm His sole lordship?

The First Proof: No False God Has Manifested Signs of Divinity
Imam Maturidi argues from absence of divine evidence and unimpeded prophetic miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Maturidi's argument that the lack of evidence from false gods and the unimpeded miracles of the prophets prove the oneness of the true God.

Core Idea
The absence of divine acts from other gods, and the unhindered miracles of prophets, prove tawhid.

Imam Maturidi begins his proof for tawhid by examining the claims of other so-called gods. He points out that no other deity has ever presented a divine act or sent messengers with miracles. Moreover, the prophets' miracles, which any rival god would have obstructed, were not prevented, confirming that there is no partner with Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to grasp the flow. Notice the phrase 'لم يذكر عن غير الإله' which sets the premise that no other god has claimed divinity with evidence.
2
Identify the two parts of the proof
The proof consists of (a) the lack of evidence from false gods, and (b) the non-prevention of prophets' miracles. The second part is introduced by 'وأيضا'.
Pay attention to the transition.
3
Understand the argument from prevention
Reflect on the logic: if another god existed, he would have prevented the prophets from manifesting miracles to protect his own divinity. Since no prevention occurred, no such god exists.
This is the key rhetorical move.
4
Apply the conclusion
The passage ends by affirming that the true God is al-Wahid al-Qahhar, who subdues all obstinate opponents. This reinforces the monotheistic conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد، فإنه لم يذكر عن غير الإله الذي يعرفه أهل التوحيد دعوى الإلهية والإشارة إلى أثر فعل منه يدل على ربوبيته، ولا وجد في شيء معنى أمكن إخراجه عن حمله، ولا بعث رسلا بالآيات التي تقهر العقول ويبهر لها، فتثبت أن القول بذلك خيال ووسواس. وأيضا [؟] الرسل بالآيات التي يضطر من شهدها أنها فعل من لو كان معه شريك ليمنعهم عن إظهارها؛ إذ بذلك إبطال ربوبيتهم وألوهيتهم، فإذ لم يوجد ولا معوا عن ذلك مع كثرة المكابرين والمعاندين ممن لو أحبوا وجود الإبدار لهم في إظهار أيامهم لوجدوا - فثبت أن ذلك إنما سليم للرسل؛ لما يكن الإله الحق والخالق للخلق غير الواحد القهار الذي قهر كل متعنت متعنت مكابر عن التمويه فضلا من التحقيق، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And after, no one besides the God whom the people of tawhid know has claimed divinity and pointed to a trace of an act from Him indicating His lordship. Nor was there found in anything a meaning that could be taken out of its import, nor did He send messengers with signs that overwhelm minds and dazzle them, so it is established that the claim of that is fantasy and delusion. And also the messengers with the signs that compel whoever witnesses them that it is an act that, if there were a partner with Him, would prevent them from manifesting them; for by that is the invalidation of their lordship and divinity. So since it was not found, and they were not prevented from that despite the abundance of the obstinate and the stubborn, who if they had loved the existence of an opportunity for themselves in manifesting their days they would have found, then it is established that that is only safe for the messengers because the true God and Creator of creation is none other than the One, the Subduer, who subdued every obstinate and stubborn one from mere deception, let alone the truth. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 619

Commentary
This passage is a polemical proof for tawhid. Imam Maturidi begins by stating that no claimant to divinity other than the true God has ever provided evidence—whether a claimed divine act or a meaningful sign. He then argues that the prophets were sent with overwhelming miracles, and the very fact that these miracles were not prevented by any supposed partner demonstrates that no such partner exists. If there had been another god, he would have obstructed the prophets' miracles to protect his own divinity. The fact that they were not obstructed, despite many enemies who would have loved to find a way to stop them, proves that the prophets were granted these signs solely by the one true God. The passage concludes that the real God is the One Subduer who humbles all obstinate opponents.

Key Terms
التوحيد
الإلهية
الربوبية
الآيات
الواحد القهار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think this proof relies solely on empirical observation of miracles, but it actually uses the argument from prevention (if a partner existed, he would have prevented the miracles).
Correction: The key logic is that the lack of obstruction of prophets' miracles proves the nonexistence of any competing deity, not just that miracles occurred.

Checkpoint
What is the main argument in this passage regarding the existence of other gods?
A) Other gods have not appeared because they do not exist.
B) The prophets' miracles were not prevented, proving no partner exists to stop them.
C) The Quran explicitly states there is only one God.
D) Reason alone proves multiplicity is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The lack of divine acts from other claimants and the unimpeded miracles of the prophets collectively prove that there is no god but Allah, the One, the Subduer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim that no partner exists with Allah, yet do you sometimes rely on your own strength, wealth, or status as if they have independent power? What would it mean to truly submit to the One Subduer in your daily decisions?
?
The passage says the obstinate ones would have loved to find a way to stop the prophets. Reflect: Do you secretly wish for a justification to avoid obeying Allah in a particular area of your life? How does the impossibility of such justification move you to surrender?
?
If the prophets' miracles were unimpeded because no partner exists, what does that say about the excuses you make when you hesitate to follow the truth? Are you, in your heart, postulating a 'partner' that isn't there?

Proof from Necessity of Showing Divine Acts
Maturidi argues that if another god existed, he would have shown his acts; their absence proves oneness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof from the necessity of each god displaying his own acts, and how its absence proves the oneness of God.

Core Idea
If a second god existed, he would have shown his own creation – since none is seen, God is one.

Imam Maturidi presents another compelling rational argument for tawhid. He builds on the logical expectation that a true god would necessarily demonstrate his power through distinct acts of creation. Since we observe only one consistent system of creation, we conclude that there is only one Creator. This lesson unpacks that argument and its Quranic support.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation once to get the overall argument. Notice the conditional structure: 'if there were ... then ...'.
There is an unclear word in the Arabic; do not let it distract you.
2
Identify the core argument
The passage begins with a conditional: if another god existed, he would have displayed his wisdom and separated his acts. Since he did not, it proves God's uniqueness.
This is a modus tollens logical form.
3
Examine the Quranic citations
Maturidi quotes Quran 23:91 and 13:16 to support his argument. Look at the quoted verses and see how they reinforce the idea that each god would take his own creation.
4
Reflect on the implication of agreement (iṣṭilāḥ)
The passage adds that if multiple gods existed, they would need to agree, which implies incapability and ignorance – impossible for a true deity.
This shows the absurdity of polytheism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أنه لو كان مع الله إله لأظهر الآخر حكمته وفصل فعله من فعل [؟] الله الحق ليعلم به قدرته وسلطانه، فإذ لم يفعل بان أن الله المتوحد بالإلهية والمتفرد بالربوبية، وذلك معنى قوله : وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُ مِنْ إِله إِذًا لَذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِله بِمَا خَلَقَ ، وكذلك قوله : أَمْ جَعَلُوا لِلهِ شُرَكَاءَ خَلَقُوا كَخَلْقِهِ. ثم وجه الإصطلاح يدل على العجز والجهل ، مع ما لو كان كذلك لم يكن الأمر الواحد في نسبه الخلق وتحقيقه له إلا من حيث يقهرهم ويدخلهم تحت قدرته وصنعه ، والله الموفق.
And also that if there were with God a god, the other would have displayed his wisdom and separated his act from the act of [؟] the true God so that His power and authority would be known. Since he did not do so, it became clear that God is unique in divinity and singular in lordship. That is the meaning of His saying: 'And there was no god with Him; then each god would have taken what he created.' And likewise His saying: 'Or have they assigned to Allah partners who created like His creation?' Then the aspect of agreement indicates incapability and ignorance. Moreover, if it were so, the sole command in attributing creation and realizing it to Him would only be from the aspect that He subdues them and brings them under His power and making. And Allah is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 619

Commentary
This passage presents another rational proof. Maturidi argues that if another god existed, he would necessarily demonstrate his wisdom and produce acts distinct from the true God's acts so that his power and authority would be recognized. Since no such distinct acts are observed, it is evident that God alone possesses divinity and lordship. He cites Quran 23:91 (each god would take his own creation) and Quran 13:16 (partners creating like His creation) as scriptural corroboration. Then he notes that the requirement of agreement (iṣṭilāḥ) between multiple gods implies incapability and ignorance—traits incompatible with divinity. The passage concludes that if multiple gods were possible, the attribution of creation to a single being would only be through their being subdued by Him, reinforcing His sole sovereignty.

Key Terms
أظهر الآخر
المتوحد بالإلهية
المتفرد بالربوبية
وجه الإصطلاح
العجز والجهل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The absence of other gods' acts is an argument from silence that proves nothing.
Correction: Maturidi argues that a true god would necessarily display his acts; the absence is not silence but evidence that no other god exists.

Checkpoint
What does Imam Maturidi conclude from the fact that no other god has displayed his own acts?
A) Other gods exist but are hiding.
B) God is unique in divinity and singular in lordship.
C) The created world is not sufficient evidence.
D) Prophets are the only way to know God.

Key Takeaway
The absence of any distinct creative acts from another god demonstrates that Allah alone is the true deity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof is not just abstract; it calls you to look at the world around you. When you see the sky, the earth, your own body—do you ever catch yourself attributing their order to chance or secondary causes? If this argument convinces you that no other hand is visible, what would it mean for you to live each day as if Allah alone is the sole provider and controller? Will you pause today and thank Him for a specific blessing, acknowledging that only He could have brought it about?
?
Maturidi says that if there were another god, he would have 'separated his act' from Allah's. But you have moments where you try to separate areas of your life—like work or relationships—from Allah's claim. Where in your life do you still act as if there is a 'separate domain' that Allah does not rule? What would it take for you to submit that area fully to His lordship?
?
The aspect of agreement between multiple gods would indicate ignorance and incapability. Think about your own decisions: do you sometimes seek approval from others as if they were 'co-deities' in your life? Whose opinion do you fear or prioritize more than Allah's? How does this proof challenge you to recognize that seeking agreement from created beings can reveal your own weakness, while submitting solely to Allah is true power?

The Cosmic Order Proves the Oneness of God
Maturidi enumerates cosmic phenomena to prove one manager.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the unified management of the cosmos—seasons, rainfall, celestial bodies, and sustenance—necessitates a single Creator.

Core Idea
The coherent, interdependent design of creation demands one Director.

Imam Maturidi presents a compelling teleological argument from the observable order and interconnectedness of the universe. He points to the consistent patterns in seasons, weather, celestial movements, and the provision of food for all creatures. Since all these phenomena operate on a single, harmonious plan, they cannot be the work of multiple gods. This passage lays out that reasoning clearly.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Notice the list of phenomena Maturidi enumerates.
The Arabic uses rhetorical repetition to emphasize unity.
2
Identify the core logical structure
The argument is: if multiple managers existed, the unified system would be disrupted. But we see unity, so there must be one manager.
3
Reflect on the interconnectedness
Consider how seasons, rain, and sustenance are linked. This interdependence is key to the argument.
Maturidi shows that these cannot be divided among multiple gods.
4
Summarize the conclusion
The conclusion is that 'القول بالواحد' (affirmation of the One) is necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما دلالة الاستدلال بالخلق فهو أنه لو كان أكثر فيهم التدبير نحو أن تحول الأزمنة من الشتاء والصيف ، أو تحول خروج الإنزال وينعها أو تقدير السماء والأرض ، أو تسيير الشمس والقمر والنجوم ، أو أغذية الخلق أو تدبير معاش جواهر الحيوان . فإذ دار كله على مسلك واحد ، ونوع من التدبير : وانساق ذلك على سنن واحد ، لا يتم بمديرين ؛ لذلك لزم القول بالواحد. وبالله التوفيق .. والثاني أن الأجناس على اختلافها وتباعد ما بينها من نحو السماء والأرض وأطراف الأرض ، وجعل أرزاق أهلها متصلة بالمنافع ، حتى كان كل أنواع [؟].
As for the evidence of deduction from creation: it is that if there were more than one in the management—such as the change of seasons from winter and summer, or the change of the coming of rain and its cessation, or the determination of the sky and the earth, or the movement of the sun, moon, and stars, or the nourishment of creatures, or the management of the livelihood of animate beings—since all of this follows one course and one type of management, and it proceeds according to one way, it is not completed by two managers; therefore, the assertion of the One is necessary. And with Allah is success. And the second: that the species, despite their differences and the vastness between them—such as the sky and the earth and the extremities of the earth, and the making of the provisions of its people connected to benefits, until every type [؟].
Source pages p. 620

Commentary
This passage presents a teleological argument from the order of creation. Maturidi enumerates various phenomena that exhibit a single, consistent pattern: the change of seasons, rainfall patterns, the design of the heavens and earth, the movements of celestial bodies, the provision of sustenance, and the management of animal livelihoods. He argues that all these processes follow one course (maslak wāḥid) and one system, and such unified management cannot be the work of multiple directors. Hence, it is necessary to affirm the oneness of God. He then begins a second point about the diversity of species and their interconnected provisions, but the text breaks off. The overall argument is that the coherence and interdependence of creation point to a single, wise Creator.

Key Terms
دلالة الاستدلال بالخلق
التدبير
مسلك واحد
سنن واحد
القول بالواحد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Multiple gods could divide the tasks (e.g., one for seasons, one for stars).
Correction: Maturidi shows that all phenomena are interconnected (e.g., rain affects agriculture, seasons affect animal life) and follow one coherent plan, which cannot be the work of multiple independent directors.

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence Maturidi presents from creation for God's oneness?
A) The complexity of creation.
B) The diversity of species.
C) The unified pattern in natural phenomena.
D) The inability of humans to create.

Key Takeaway
The unified order of creation—from seasons to sustenance—logically requires a single Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the changing seasons, the rain, or the movement of the stars, do you consciously see them as signs pointing to one Manager, or do you take them for granted? How would your awareness of Allah change if you made this connection daily?
?
The passage says all of creation runs on a single course under one management. Where in your life do you still act as if your affairs are independent, as if you are your own manager? What would it look like to submit that area fully to the One Director?
?
If the unified order demands one Creator, then every natural event—including the provision you receive—is from Him. Reflect on a recent blessing you attributed to your own effort. How can you shift your gratitude from yourself to the One who orchestrated it?

The Proof from Mutual Hindrance (Tamānuʿ)
Maturidi refutes polytheism by logical deduction from mutual hindrance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof of mutual hindrance (tamānuʿ) that demonstrates the impossibility of multiple gods.

Core Idea
Multiple gods inevitably lead to contradiction or impotence, so only One God can exist.

Imam Maturidi presents a rational argument drawn from the Quran to prove that God must be one. The proof of mutual hindrance (tamānuʿ) examines what would happen if two or more gods existed, showing that every possibility leads to an absurdity. This lesson walks you through the argument's logical steps and its Quranic basis.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Quranic foundation
Read the two Quranic verses Maturidi cites. They imply that if multiple gods existed, each would claim exclusive creation, leading to conflict.
These verses are the springboard for the rational argument.
2
Grasp the logical trilemma
Maturidi outlines three possibilities for two gods: both have equal power, both are powerless, or one is powerful and the other weak. Each leads to an absurdity.
This trilemma exhausts all logical scenarios.
3
Explore the implications of each scenario
If both are powerful, they would thwart each other, causing contradiction. If both are powerless, they cannot be gods. If one is powerful, the other is a subject, not a god.
4
See how the argument eliminates polytheism
The only coherent conclusion is that there is one God who possesses all power and knowledge of the unseen.
This proof is a cornerstone of Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الله الحق ليعلم به قدرته وسلطانه، فإذ لم يفعل بان أن الله المتوحد بالإلهية والمتفرد بالربوبية، وذلك معنى قوله: وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُ مِنْ إِله إِذًا لَذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِله بِمَا خَلَقَ، وكذلك قوله: أَمْ جَعَلُوا لِلهِ شُرَكَاءَ خَلَقُوا كَخَلْقِهِ. ثم وجه الإصطلاح يدل على العجز والجهل، مع ما لو كان كذلك لم يكن الأمر الواحد في نسبه الخلق وتحقيقه له إلا من حيث يقهرهم ويدخلهم تحت قدرته وصنعه، والله الموفق. وأيضا أنه لو كان مع الله إله لا يخلو من أن يقدر على فعل يسره من الآخر أو لا، وكذلك الله سبحانه منه، فإن قدرا جميعا ملك كل واحد منها تجهيل الآخر، وفي ذلك زوال الربوبية، وإن لم يقدرا عجز كل واحد منها، والعجز يُسقط الألوهية، أو قدر أحدهما دون الآخر فهو الرب والآخر مربوب، مع ما كان علم الغيب علم الربوبية، فمن ليس له فهو مربوب. ثم لا يخلو أيضا من قدرة كل واحد منها على غيره في منع ما يروم الفعل بغيره ويريده أو لا، القدرة وتحقيق عجز وذلك يسقط الربوبية، كل [؟] فيكون فيها إمكان خروج أو يقدر الواحد خاصة فيكون هو الرب سبحانه.
Allah, the Truth, that His power and authority may be known. When He does not do so, it becomes clear that Allah is unique in divinity and singular in lordship. That is the meaning of His statement: 'And there was no god with Him; otherwise each god would have taken away what he created.' And likewise His statement: 'Or have they attributed to Allah partners who created like His creation?' Then the mode of implication indicates incapacity and ignorance. Moreover, if it were such, the single matter in attributing creation and realizing it to Him is only through His overwhelming them and bringing them under His power and making. And Allah grants success. And also: if there were a god with Allah, it is unavoidable that either each is able to do what it pleases from the other or not, and likewise Allah, exalted, from him. If both are able, each of them would possess the means to outwit the other, and in that is the annulment of lordship. If both are unable, each of them is powerless, and powerlessness negates divinity. Or if one of them is able to the exclusion of the other, then it is the Lord and the other is a subject, especially since knowledge of the unseen is knowledge of lordship, so whoever does not have it is a subject. Also, it is unavoidable that each of them has power over the other to prevent what it intends and desires, or not. Power and the realization of powerlessness annul lordship. All [?], so that possibility of exit applies, or the one alone is able, so He is the Lord, exalted.
Source pages p. 620

Commentary
This passage presents the classical kalam proof of mutual hindrance (tamānuʿ) for the oneness of God. It begins by referencing two Quranic verses that imply that if multiple gods existed, each would claim exclusive creation, leading to conflict. Maturidi then argues rationally: if there were two gods, three possibilities exist. First, if both have equal power, each would try to thwart the other's will, causing contradiction in the world order and invalidating lordship. Second, if both are powerless, they cannot be gods. Third, if one is powerful and the other weak, the weak one is a subject, not a god. Additionally, knowledge of the unseen is a necessary attribute of divinity, and only one can possess it. The argument concludes that only one God can truly be the Lord.

Key Terms
التمانع
الإلهية
الربوبية
العجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is a straw man argument.
Correction: Maturidi's argument exhausts all logical possibilities for multiple gods, showing each leads to an absurdity, making it a sound refutation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's tamānuʿ argument, what happens if two gods both have equal power?
A) They cooperate harmoniously
B) Each would try to outwit the other, causing contradiction
C) One would submit to the other
D) The world would be perfectly ordered

Key Takeaway
The tamānuʿ argument proves that only One God can be truly divine because multiple gods would either conflict or be powerless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the logical proof of mutual hindrance is so clear, why do you still sometimes hesitate in your conviction that Allah is One? Where does that hesitation come from in your heart?
?
The proof shows that any partner would be either powerless or a subject. When you sin, are you not, in that moment, acting as if another 'power' can benefit or harm you outside of Allah's will? What does that say about your understanding of tawḥīd?
?
You have just studied that multiple gods are logically impossible. Now, look at your life: are there multiple 'gods'—things you ultimate serve or rely on besides Allah? How will you dismantle them starting today?

Allah's Existence
beginner
4 min
The First Proof: Unity of Natural Processes
Maturidi presents the first proof from the unity of natural processes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consistent patterns of natural phenomena like seasons and rainfall point to a single Creator.

Core Idea
Harmony in nature requires a single manager.

Imam Maturidi begins by drawing our attention to the observable order in the world. The changing seasons, the rainfall, the movements of celestial bodies – all follow a uniform pattern. Such consistency cannot be the product of multiple independent agents, for they would inevitably conflict. This simple observation forms the first pillar of the proof from creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice how Maturidi lists several natural processes that all follow a single course.
The list includes seasons, rainfall, heavens/earth, sun/moon/stars, sustenance.
2
Understand the key concept
Identify the concept of 'tadbir' (management) and how Maturidi argues that a single management system cannot be run by two managers.
Think of it as two captains trying to steer one ship.
3
Reflect on the logical implication
Ask yourself: If there were two gods, would creation exhibit such harmony? Maturidi says no. Conclude that only one God can exist.
This is a logical inference from observed unity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما دلالة الاستدلال بالخلق فهو أنه لو كان أكثر فيهم التدبير نحو أن تحول الأزمنة من الشتاء والصيف، أو تحول خروج الإنزال وينعها أو تقدير السماء والأرض، أو تسيير الشمس والقمر والنجوم، أو أغذية الخلق أو تدبير معاش جواهر الحيوان. فإذ دار كله على مسلك واحد، ونوع من التدبير : وانساق ذلك على سنن واحد، لا يتم بمديرين؛ لذلك لزم القول بالواحد وبالله التوفيق. والثاني أن الأجناس على اختلافها وتباعد ما بينها من نحو السماء والأرض وأطراف الأرض، وجعل أرزاق أهلها متصلة بالمنافع، حتى كان كل أنواع الخارج جميع [؟] تارج من الأرنس [؟] يكون بأسباب السماء، وحاجات كل أهل البلدان منتشرة في الأطراف، ومعاش البشر مجعول في أنواع الكاسب، على هذاا أمر الجميع فلو كان ذلك لعدد، لم يحتمل أن ترجع منافعها إلى من له العالم من الخلق على اختلاف العالم. ثبت أن مدير ذلك كله واحد. وعلى ما ذكرت، الأوقات الليل والنهار والساعات. ودخول بعض في بعض على قدر الحاجات، وهذا والله أعلم - عنى قوله: ما ترى في خلق الرحمن من تفاوت، فهذا مع ما جعلت ما الأعيان، على جهات ست، ثبت أن مدير كل - على اختلاف الأجسام، وهي الأجناس كل تحت معنى واحدة ولا قوة إلا بالله واجد، حتى
As for the evidence of inference from creation, it is that if there were multiple managers regarding the shifting of seasons from winter to summer, the changing of rainfall and its withholding, the determination of heaven and earth, the course of the sun, moon, and stars, the sustenance of creatures, or the management of animal livelihoods – since all of it runs on one course and one type of management, and flows on a single path, it cannot be accomplished by two managers. Therefore, it is necessary to affirm the One, and with Allah is success. The second is that the species, despite their differences and distances – as with heaven, earth, and the corners of the earth – and that He made the provisions of their inhabitants connected with benefits, until all types of exteriors [؟] from the sky, and the needs of all people of the lands are spread in the regions, and human livelihood is placed in types of earnings – upon this is the order of all. If it were from multiple, it would not be possible for benefits to return to whomever owns the world of creation, given the differences of the world. It is established that the manager of all that is one. And as I mentioned, the times – night, day, and hours – and the entering of some into others according to need – and this, Allah knows best – refers to His statement: 'You see no disparity in the creation of the Beneficent.' Thus, with what I have set of the essences in six directions, it is established that the manager of everything, despite the differences of bodies and species, is under one meaning, and there is no power except with Allah, the One, until
Source pages p. 620

Commentary
This passage presents two interconnected proofs for the oneness of God from the observation of creation. The first proof focuses on the unity of natural processes: the changing of seasons, rainfall, celestial motions, and sustenance all follow a single consistent pattern. Such harmony cannot arise from multiple independent managers, because each would introduce its own system leading to conflict. Therefore, only one Manager is possible. The second proof considers the interdependence of different regions and species: the provisions of distant lands are connected via means from the sky, and human livelihoods are distributed across various earnings. Despite geographic and biological diversity, all needs are met in a coordinated way. If there were multiple gods, this interconnected system would break down. The Quranic verse 'You see no disparity in the creation of the Beneficent' is cited to reinforce the argument. The passage concludes that the manager of all things, despite differences in bodies and species, is one.

Key Terms
الاستدلال بالخلق (istidlāl bi-l-khalq)
التدبير (tadbīr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why can't the observed unity in nature be the work of two managers?
A) Because they would cooperate
B) Because they would be in conflict
C) Because nature runs on its own
D) Because humans manage it

Key Takeaway
The consistency of natural processes proves that they are managed by a single Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness the changing seasons or the rising of the sun, do you consciously recognize the hand of a single Manager, or do you attribute it to impersonal forces? How does your answer change your sense of accountability to Allah today?
?
Maturidi argues that consistency in nature cannot be from multiple managers. In your own life, do you try to serve multiple masters—pleasure, status, wealth—and expect harmony? How does the oneness of Allah call you to abandon that divided loyalty?
?
If the entire universe follows a single course under one Manager, what does that imply about the purpose of your existence? Are you living in alignment with that single purpose, or are you scattered in multiple directions? What will you do to refocus?
